[HEADING] Project Abstract

[TEXT] PROJECT ABSTRACT Project Title: Advance Community Health Inc - Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition (SAC) Applicant Org Name: Advance Community Health, Inc. Address: 1001 Rock Quarry Rd, Raleigh, NC 27610-3825 Project Director: Scot N. McCray Phone Number: (919) 250-2923 E-Mail Address: scmccray@advancechc.org Web: www.advancechc.org Federal Request: HRSA-26-004, Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition (SAC), $4,725,281 annually Type(s) of Section 330 Funding Requested: CHC, HCH SAC ID, CITY, and STATE OF THE SERVICE AREA: ID 137; Raleigh, NC Patient Target: 23,691 patients; increased to 56,003 patients (including CHC, HCH) Funding Preference: MUA/MUP and HPSA - Medical, Dental, and Behavioral Health Advance Community Health, Inc. (ACH), formerly known as Wake Health Services, is a private, nonprofit, Health Center Program (HCP) grantee funded under Section 330(e) as a Community Health Center and Section 330(h) as a Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Program. ACH proudly serves Wake and Franklin Counties, North Carolina, operating twelve permanent service delivery sites, one administrative/service delivery site, one mobile unit, and one administrative office to maximize access across the service area.Since its founding more than 50-years ago, ACH has remained steadfast in its mission to meet the health care needs of its communities and has become a trusted and vital patient-centered medical home throughout the region. ACH ensures that all required services are available to patients either directly or through formal referral arrangements. These services include General Primary Care, Diagnostic Laboratory, Diagnostic Radiology, Screenings, Coverage for Emergencies During and After Hours, Voluntary Family Planning, Immunizations, Well Child Services, Gynecological Care, Obstetrical - Prenatal, Intrapartum, and Postpartum, Dental - Preventive, Pharmaceutical Services, Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Required Substance Use Disorder Services, Case/Care Management, Eligibility Assistance, Health Education, Outreach, Transportation, and Translation. In addition, ACH provides a range of additional services designed to meet community-identified needs and further improve patient outcomes. These include Additional Dental Services, Mental Health Services, Environmental Health Services, Nutrition, and Additional Enabling/Supportive Services. ACH also provides psychiatry services as a specialty service. Aligning with the Make America Healthy Again (MAHA) initiative to advance national health equity and prevention goals - ACH projects continued growth in the number of unduplicated patients served across all service types listed in the SAAT, building on its consistent upward trend in UDS performance. Based on population health needs and prior utilization patterns, ACH anticipates serving approximately 56,003 unduplicated patients in the upcoming project year

[TEXT] – 55,103 CHC patients and 900 HCH patients. This projection reflects both the continuation of existing patient demand and the planned expansion of enabling services, outreach, and access initiatives identified through the most recent Community Health Needs Assessment. In 2024, ACH served 21,538 unduplicated patients, including 870 individuals experiencing

[TEXT] Project Narrative Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[HEADING] INTRODUCTION

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. (ACH), formerly known as Wake Health Services, is a private, nonprofit, Health Center Program (HCP) grantee funded under Section 330(e) as a Community Health Center and Section 330(h) as a Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Program. ACH proudly serves Wake and Franklin Counties, North Carolina, operating twelve permanent service delivery sites, one administrative/service delivery site, one mobile unit, and one administrative office to maximize access across the service area.

[TEXT] Since its founding more than 50-years ago, ACH has remained steadfast in its mission to meet the health care needs of its communities and has become a trusted and vital patient-centered medical home throughout the region.

[TEXT] MISSION To deliver quality, compassionate primary health care - every patient, every time - in response to the needs of our communities.

[TEXT] VISION We are a model of affordable health care and a trusted partner, building healthy communities, one patient at a time.

[TEXT] ACH fulfills this mission with the highest ethical standards and unwavering commitment to equitable access - regardless of ability to pay, insurance status, or income. ACH is dedicated to providing patient-centered, accessible, cost-effective, and timely primary health care for all, recognizing that access to quality medical care is essential to the overall health of the community.

[TEXT] The purpose of ACH is to provide comprehensive, coordinated, and community-responsive primary health care services by:

[TEXT] · Assisting residents in accessing medical, dental, behavioral health, and pharmaceutical care through individualized education and advocacy;

[TEXT] · Helping patients develop personal health care plans while facilitating coordination among all providers and services in the community; and

[TEXT] · Reducing the economic burden of care for low-income, underserved, and uninsured residents.

[TEXT] ACH serves as a vital access point for medically underserved residents across the service area. The organization's care delivery model is built on reducing health disparities, increasing access to essential services, and eliminating barriers to comprehensive care. ACH's family- and community-oriented approach ensures the delivery of integrated services across all stages of life - from pediatrics to geriatrics - promoting continuity of care, patient trust, and improved long-term outcomes.

[TEXT] ACH ensures that all required services are available to patients either directly or through formal referral arrangements. These services include General Primary Care, Diagnostic Laboratory, Diagnostic Radiology, Screenings, Coverage for Emergencies During and After Hours, Voluntary Family Planning, Immunizations, Well Child Services, Gynecological Care, Obstetrical - Prenatal, Intrapartum, and Postpartum, Dental - Preventive, Pharmaceutical Services, Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Required Substance Use

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] 2

[TEXT] In addition, ACH provides a range of additional services designed to meet community-identified needs and further improve patient outcomes. These include Additional Dental Services, Mental Health Services, Environmental Health Services, Nutrition, and Additional Enabling/Supportive Services. ACH also provides psychiatry services as a specialty service.

[TEXT] ACH aligns with the Make America Healthy Again (MAHA) initiative to advance national health equity and prevention goals. Through MAHA-aligned programs, ACH expands access to primary care, chronic disease management, and community-based education focused on nutrition, physical activity, and behavioral health. This initiative supports HRSA's priorities to reduce health disparities, prevent avoidable hospitalizations, and improve population health outcomes across medically underserved areas in both rural and urban communities throughout the United States.

[TEXT] ACH continues to meet all performance standards established by the Health Resources and Services Administration (HRSA) and the Department of Health and Human Services, while expanding medical services and adding new programs to meet emerging needs. In September 2024, ACH successfully completed a HRSA Operational Site Visit (OSV) under the HRSA Health Center Compliance Manual.

[TEXT] With more than 65,000 annual patient visits and a half-century legacy of service, ACH continues to transform lives and strengthen community health outcomes. Its unwavering commitment to affordability, accessibility, and quality care has earned ACH its role as a trusted community health partner and essential provider throughout Wake and Franklin Counties.

[TEXT] All services are consistent with those listed on Form 5A: Services Provided.

[HEADING] NEED

[TEXT] 1. Describe the proposed service area (consistent with Attachment 1: Service Area Map and Table), including:

[TEXT] a. The service area boundaries.

[TEXT] The proposed service area for Advance Community Health encompasses Franklin and Wake Counties in the eastern Piedmont region of North Carolina. Both counties are designated in whole or in part as Medically Underserved Areas (MUA) and Health Professional Shortage Areas (HPSA), underscoring the critical need for expanded access to comprehensive primary care. The service area boundaries are drawn to include populations most affected by poverty, uninsured status, chronic disease, and limited access to private providers. These boundaries align with ACH's service delivery sites and ensure coverage across both urban and rural communities.

[TEXT] Wake County represents one of the most urbanized and rapidly growing regions in North Carolina, home to Raleigh, the state capital, and part of the Research Triangle Park. Population growth, density, and economic expansion have created increasing demand for affordable, accessible health services - particularly among low-income and uninsured residents. Between 2010 and 2020, Wake County's population increased by more than 25%, with continuing growth projected through 2030. Source(s): Carolina Demography; University of North Carolina, 2022.

[TEXT] Franklin County, by contrast, is a smaller, rural county northeast of Wake. With limited transportation infrastructure - only two major U.S. highways - residents face barriers in reaching health care services. Many Franklin County residents commute to Wake County for employment, education, and care, highlighting the importance of ACH's integrated service delivery across county lines. The county's health system capacity is limited, with higher poverty rates and fewer providers per capita than the state average.

[TEXT] Population Profile. The total service area population is 1,246,256, reflecting a 27.6% increase since 2010. Approximately 94% of residents live in Wake County, while Franklin County - though smaller shows concentrated need related to poverty, chronic disease, and transportation. The target population, defined as individuals living below 200% of the Federal Poverty Guidelines (FPG), totals 254,844 residents (20.5%) of the service area population. Source(s): U.S. Census 2010; ACS 2016-2020; Health Center Program GeoCare Navigator, October 2025.

[TEXT] The shortage of health care professionals and lack of access to care across the Franklin-Wake County service area continues to demonstrate the significant unmet medical, dental, and behavioral health needs among residents.

[TEXT] In Franklin County, the population-to-primary care physician ratio is 14,910:1, more than 10 times higher than the state ratio of 1,410:1 and the national ratio of 1,310:1. Access to dental care is equally limited, with a population-to-dentist ratio of 8,560:1 compared to 1,610:1 statewide. Mental health shortages are also acute, with a ratio of 720:1 - more than twice the state average of 290:1.

[TEXT] By comparison, Wake County, which includes the urban Raleigh area, has significantly greater provider density, with a 1,150:1 population-to-primary care physician ratio, 1,320:1 for dentists, and 220:1 for mental health providers. However, even in Wake County, low-income and uninsured residents continue to face barriers to timely and affordable care, particularly in high-need zip codes and among underinsured populations.

[TEXT] c. How the boundaries of the service area ensure that services are available and accessible to the residents of the area.

[TEXT] ACH defines its service area boundaries to align with the geographic regions where the greatest concentrations of medically underserved residents live, work, and seek care. The service area reflects the locations of ACH's clinical sites, the transportation patterns of patients, and the distribution of populations experiencing the highest levels of health disparities.

[TEXT] · Geographic Alignment: The boundaries encompass neighborhoods and counties designated as MUA and HPSA, ensuring ACH services are targeted to communities with the greatest unmet need.

[TEXT] · Proximity to Care: Clinical sites are strategically located within residential communities, near public transportation routes, and in areas accessible to patients traveling from rural areas. This ensures that residents can reach services without undue travel burden.

[TEXT] . Population Reach: The service area boundary captures both urban and rural populations that rely on ACH as their primary health care home. It includes low-income families, agricultural workers, and uninsured or underinsured individuals who face significant barriers to accessing private or specialty care.

[TEXT] · Accessibility Supports: Enabling services - including transportation assistance, care management, and translation - extend access to patients throughout the service area, ensuring that geography does not prevent residents from obtaining care. ACH also extends access through telehealth visits and after- hours on-call coverage, ensuring 24/7 access to clinical guidance.

[TEXT] By intentionally defining the service area to match population need, transportation access, and site placement, ACH ensures that comprehensive, patient-centered services are available and accessible to all residents within its service area boundaries.

[TEXT] d. How the overlap of political subdivisions, school districts, and areas served by Federal and State health and social programs affect access to primary health care services in the service area.

[TEXT] ACH serves a defined service area where political subdivisions, school districts, and state and federal health and social programs often overlap. These overlaps present both opportunities and challenges in ensuring equitable access to primary health care.

[TEXT] · Political Subdivisions: The service area includes multiple counties and municipalities with varying levels of public health infrastructure, transportation options, and funding priorities. Differences in local government resources can create uneven access to care; ACH mitigates this by ensuring consistent services across its clinical sites and providing enabling services such as transportation coordination and care management.

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242744

[TEXT] Project Narrative Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[TEXT] . School Districts: The presence of multiple school districts across the service area creates opportunities for ACH to extend pediatric and adolescent services, including school-based health initiatives, immunization partnerships, and health education. However, variations in district-level funding and resources can affect the availability of school health staff, reinforcing ACH's role as a trusted partner in ensuring children and adolescents receive preventive and primary care services.

[TEXT] . Federal and State Health and Social Programs: The service area includes populations eligible for Medicaid, Medicare, WIC, SNAP, and housing assistance programs. Program requirements, eligibility thresholds, and availability of services may vary by county or administering agency, creating complexity for patients. ACH helps patients navigate these systems through benefits counseling, application support, and referrals, ensuring that they can maximize available resources to support their health.

[TEXT] Overall, these overlaps reinforce the importance of ACH's coordinated, patient-centered model of care. By working across political boundaries, partnering with multiple school systems, and integrating with state and federal social service programs, ACH reduces fragmentation and ensures that all residents in the service area can access comprehensive, high-quality primary care, regardless of where they live or which jurisdiction they fall under.

[TEXT] e. How you will annually review the proposed service area to identify where your patients reside, available health resources, and unmet need.

[TEXT] ACH conducts an annual review of its service area to ensure alignment between where patients reside, the availability of local health resources, and emerging areas of unmet need. Following submission of the annual Uniform Data System (UDS) report, ACH analyzes patient origin data by ZIP code to determine where the majority of patients live. These ZIP codes are then compared with those listed on Form 5B: Service Sites to confirm accuracy and completeness.

[TEXT] If any ZIP code representing at least 75% of ACH's total patient population is not reflected on Form 5B, ACH identifies the service site serving those patients and submits a Change in Scope request to add the ZIP code to that site. For this application, ACH also reviewed the Service Area Announcement Table (SAAT) to verify that all ZIP codes where at least 75% of patients reside are accurately represented on Form 5B.

[TEXT] Beyond ensuring scope accuracy, this annual review helps ACH monitor population shifts, evaluate areas experiencing growth or increased demand, and identify emerging service gaps. This analysis informs strategic planning, site development, and resource allocation to ensure that ACH continues to effectively meet the health care needs of residents throughout its service area. ACH is a sponsoring partner with Wake County's Community Health Needs Assessment group and uses information from the CHNA to inform services offered, hours of operation, and other identified needs.

[TEXT] g. Competing continuation applicants: Using Uniform Data System (UDS) data, describe changes to the service area since your last Service Area Competition (SAC) application.

[TEXT] Since the 2022 SAC, ACH has experienced notable demographic, utilization, and payer-mix shifts that reflect evolving community needs and ACH's success in expanding access. Source(s): UDS 2024.

[TEXT] Changes in the Service Area (Baseline UDS 2022 -> 2024)

[TEXT] · Growth and Demographics. Total patients increased by 15.2% (18,704 -> 21,538), driven primarily by children and working-age adults - evidence of successful family and youth engagement through school- and community-based outreach. The service area remains highly diverse, with racial/ethnic minority patients ~87% of those served. The Hispanic/Latino share grew from 31% to 38%, and those best served in a language other than English rose from 25.6% to 31.1%, underscoring the need for expanded bilingual staffing, interpreter services, and culturally tailored health education.

[TEXT] . Economic Vulnerability and Coverage. Nearly 99% of patients are ≤200% FPL and 86% are ≤100% FPL (+10 points since 2022), indicating heightened economic need and reliance on sliding fee and enabling services. The uninsured rate declined from 32% to 27%, while Medicaid/CHIP edged up (41.1% -> 41.4%) and other third-party coverage increased (12% -> ~20%), reflecting payer diversification and improved financial stability. The uninsured rate is also higher in Franklin County (13%) than the state (11%) and national (10%) averages, further limiting access to consistent primary and preventive care.

[TEXT] . Medicaid Expansion Impact. North Carolina's Medicaid expansion (effective Dec 1, 2023) is already reshaping the payer mix by shifting adults from uninsured to Medicaid. ACH's Outreach and Enrollment team continues assisting with applications, renewals, and benefits literacy - supporting prevention, chronic care continuity, and reduced uncompensated care.

[TEXT] · Service Utilization. Demand for comprehensive care continues to rise. Dental patients increased nearly 40% (3,054 -> 4,262) following capacity investments and targeted outreach. Behavioral health utilization also increased alongside growth in the integrated Behavioral Health model. Although the proportion of medical patients declined, overall encounters remained stable - a normalization effect as dental and BH volumes expanded and post-COVID coding stabilized.

[TEXT] · Special Populations. ACH served 870 individuals experiencing homelessness in 2024 - still substantial, though a smaller share due to total patient growth. The Health Care for the Homeless program provides mobile and on-site medical, dental, and behavioral health services, with care management for housing, employment, and recovery support. Engagement with Migratory and Seasonal Agricultural Workers (MSAW) populations rose (132 in 2024), and public-housing-associated patients increased by ~11% due to the opening of a service delivery location in 4/2024 adjacent to public housing (added ). Since 2023, school-based partnerships have expanded preventive and behavioral health access for children/adolescents.

[TEXT] · Community Health Environment. Regional population growth, private-sector workforce shortages, and persistent social risk factors (food insecurity, transportation, housing) have increased ACH's role as a safety-net provider. ACH has maintained and grown patient engagement via community partnerships, care coordination, and enabling services.

[TEXT] Source(s): UDS 2022 - 2024; County Health Rankings 2024. Data updated 09/24/2025; HRSA Data Explorer; North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services, Office of Rural Health; U.S. Census

[TEXT] 2. Describe health care needs in the announced service area, including those that you are meeting or which are met by the current Health Center Program award recipient. If your service area includes HP, RPH, and/or MSAW funding, include the needs of each special medically underserved population. Address needs related to the following:

[TEXT] Residents across ACH's Wake and Franklin County service area experience diverse and persistent health needs that reflect both urban and rural disparities. The region includes multiple Medically Underserved Areas/Populations (MUA/Ps), HPSAs, and federally designated Opportunity Zones. Despite regional economic growth, significant gaps remain in access to affordable, comprehensive, and culturally competent care - particularly among low-income, uninsured, and minority populations. ACH's integrated model of care - grounded in prevention, chronic-disease management, and behavioral health integration - addresses these disparities by ensuring that high-quality services are accessible to all residents, regardless of ability to pay.

[TEXT] Health Care for the Homeless. Wake and Franklin Counties include a substantial and growing population experiencing homelessness. The Wake County Continuum of Care identified more than 1,200 individuals in the most recent Point-in-Time count, including those living unsheltered or in emergency and transitional housing. Rising housing costs and limited affordable units have contributed to this increase. Individuals experiencing homelessness face higher rates of chronic illness, behavioral health disorders, and substance-use conditions, often complicated by limited access to hygiene, medication storage, and follow- up care.

[TEXT] ACH's Health Care for the Homeless program delivers mobile and on-site medical, dental, and behavioral health services at shelters, and outreach sites. Care management staff assist with housing applications, employment resources, and linkage to recovery and behavioral health programs. Through strong partnerships with local shelters, food pantries, and housing agencies, ACH ensures care continuity for unsheltered and temporarily housed individuals and families.

[TEXT] These activities align with HRSA's expectations for outreach and service delivery to individuals experiencing homelessness under Section 330(h).

[TEXT] a. Comprehensive primary health care services, including in-scope nutrition, chronic disease management, preventive health education, cancer screening, and mental health services.

[TEXT] ACH ensures that all required services are available to patients either directly or through formal referral arrangements. These services include General Primary Care, Diagnostic Laboratory, Diagnostic Radiology, Screenings, Coverage for Emergencies During and After Hours, Voluntary Family Planning, Immunizations, Well Child Services, Gynecological Care, Obstetrical - Prenatal, Intrapartum, and Postpartum, Dental - Preventative, Pharmaceutical Services, Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Required Substance Use Disorder Services, Case/Care Management, Eligibility Assistance, Health Education, Outreach, Transportation, and Translation.

[HEADING] Clinical Data Summary (UDS 2022-2024)

[TEXT] ACH's clinical and population health data show consistent growth in patient volume, improved performance across several preventive and chronic disease measures, and continued emphasis on closing health disparities. Total patients increased from 18,704 in 2022 to 21,538 in 2024 (+15%), reflecting both expanded access and increased community demand.

[HEADING] Chronic Disease Trends.

[TEXT] · Hypertension: Hypertension remains the most prevalent chronic condition among ACH patients. The share of adult patients diagnosed with hypertension rose slightly from 43.1% (2022) to 46.2% (2024), reflecting enhanced screening and identification efforts. Blood pressure control (<140/90 mmHg) improved significantly - from 53.3% (2022) to 62.2% (2024) - a nine-percentage-point gain in two years. This reflects successful implementation of care coordination, adherence follow-up, and clinical decision-support tools within ACH's EpicCare Ambulatory (Epic) electronic health record (EHR).

[TEXT] . Diabetes: The proportion of adults with diabetes remained stable (28.2% -> 27.2%), while those with poorly controlled A1c (>9% or no test) rose from 25.8% -> 44.2%, prompting intensified outreach, point-of-care A1c testing, and adherence counseling.

[TEXT] . Asthma: Prevalence held steady (6.6% -> 7.1%). Clinical teams monitor medication compliance and environmental triggers through integrated primary-care and behavioral health coordination.

[TEXT] . HIV: Although a small portion of total patients (0.3% -> 0.5%), the number living with HIV increased from 54 to 82, consistent with regional epidemiologic trends. ACH continues to provide screening, linkage-to-care, and care management to maintain viral suppression. To address patient needs, ACH provides access to a part-time (0.8 FTE) nurse practitioner specializing in HIV care.

[TEXT] Cardiovascular Risk Reduction. Preventive cardiovascular care indicators remain strong and show incremental improvement:

[TEXT] · Statin therapy: Increased from 76.9% (2022) to 80.6% (2024), exceeding national health-center averages.

[TEXT] · Aspirin/antiplatelet use (IVD): Stable at 80.5% -> 79.0%, reflecting sustained adherence to secondary prevention standards.

[TEXT] Preventive Health Performance. Preventive screening performance has improved markedly since 2022, supported by Epic population registries, care coordinators, and focused outreach.

[TEXT] · Cervical cancer screening: 39.0% -> 49.6% (+10.6 points)

[TEXT] · Colorectal cancer screening: 13.8% -> 25.2% (+11.4 points)

[TEXT] · Breast cancer screening: 34.1% -> 38.9% (+4.8 points)

[TEXT] · HIV screening: 38.8% -> 64.2% (+25.4 points)

[TEXT] · Depression screening and follow-up: 64.3% -> 74.9% (+10.6 points)

[TEXT] · BMI screening and follow-up: 39.2% -> 52.2% (+13 points)

[TEXT] Perinatal and Maternal Health. Prenatal care patients increased from 64 (2022) to 94 (2024) (+47%). Early entry into prenatal care (first trimester) improved from 50.0% -> 71.3%, surpassing pre-pandemic levels and ranking in the national second quartile. This progress reflects strengthened referral systems and proactive identification of pregnant patients by ACH's outreach and care coordination teams. ACH provides OB/GYN services including voluntary family planning, prenatal services, ultrasounds, and lactation services as a part of an overall comprehensive approach to addressing women's health needs (OB opened in 12/2024).

[TEXT] Behavioral Health and Integration. Behavioral health integration continues to expand. Depression screening increased to 74.9%, with improved follow-up documentation. Depression remission at 12 months reached 10.0% in 2024, showing gradual progress and highlighting the need for sustained behavioral health follow-up and telehealth therapy options.

[TEXT] ACH's performance trajectory demonstrates sustained improvement in chronic-disease control, preventive screening, and behavioral health integration. Clinical and operational teams employ Plan-Do-Study-Act (PDSA) cycles and Epic population-health dashboards to monitor outcomes, close care gaps, and guide continuous quality improvement.

[TEXT] Other indicators:

[TEXT] · Only 44% of Franklin County women and 49% of Wake County women receive annual mammography screenings, signaling persistent gaps in preventive care.

[TEXT] · Flu vaccination coverage, a proxy for preventive health engagement, stands at 53% in Franklin County and 59% in Wake County - modestly above state and national averages (51% and 48%, respectively).

[TEXT] · Preventable hospital stays remain elevated, with 3,149 per 100,000 Medicare enrollees in Franklin County and 2,399 per 100,000 in Wake County - both above or near the state (2,670) and national (2,666) averages.

[TEXT] Source(s): UDS 2022 - 2024; County Health Rankings 2024. Data updated 09/24/2025; HRSA Data Explorer; North Carolina Department of Health and Human Services, Office of Rural Health; U.S. Census Bureau (2023 ACS); University of Wisconsin Population Health Institute; Robert Wood Johnson Foundation.

[TEXT] coordination services that can address health-related social factors such as those related to food insecurity, housing insecurity, and financial strain).

[TEXT] Many ACH patients face socioeconomic barriers that affect access to and continuity of care. High rates of poverty, limited transportation, housing instability, and food insecurity are common across the service area. ACH provides a comprehensive array of enabling and patient-support services to mitigate these barriers.

[TEXT] Each patient completes an annual social drivers of health assessment through the EHR. Identified needs - such as food insecurity, financial strain, or transportation challenges - trigger immediate connections to enabling-service staff or community partners. Patients receive assistance with insurance enrollment, transportation coordination, care management, and linkage to social-service programs.

[TEXT] Every patient requiring enhanced support is assigned a care coordinator or care manager who helps navigate medical, behavioral, and community resources. Care managers focus on clinical goals, while coordinators guide patients and families to need support, including vouchers for healthy food, housing resources, and job training opportunities. ACH's care management continuum extends into home and community settings, ensuring post-hospital follow-up and continuity for high-risk or chronically ill patients.

[TEXT] Since January through October 2025, ACH staff delivered more than 10,800 enabling and supportive service encounters to ACH patients - strengthening access, improving care coordination, and addressing social drivers of health.

[TEXT] These services - beyond required case management - have provided patients with critical connections to non-medical, social, and educational resources, including transportation, food access, Medicaid eligibility, and health education. Notably, the largest areas of impact include:

[TEXT] · Coordinating care and transitions across settings (4,014 encounters), ensuring continuity after hospital or specialty visits.

[TEXT] · Health and wellness outreach (2,043 calls) to support preventive care and patient engagement.

[TEXT] · Case management and care gap outreach (1,578 combined encounters) to address chronic disease management, missed visits, and preventive screenings.

[TEXT] · Transportation assistance (391 encounters) to remove access barriers for medically underserved patients.

[TEXT] Additional services include language interpretation, clinical pharmacist interventions, and group education sessions, reflecting ACH's comprehensive, patient-centered approach.

[TEXT] These results underscore ACH's ability to rapidly deploy enabling services infrastructure, integrate outreach and care coordination functions, and meet HRSA expectations for comprehensive, accessible, and equitable care across the expanded service area.

[TEXT] 3. Describe any recent or potential changes in the local health care landscape and how those changes may affect the needs of the target population.

[TEXT] The ACH service area is amid massive shifts that impact patient access, our workforce, and sustainability.

[TEXT] North Carolina Medicaid Expansion. The 2023 decision to expand Medicaid in NC began a flurry of activity to increase health care access to eligible patients has served as the catalyst for current and potential changes in Wake and Franklin Counties. The biggest change is patient demand for accessible and affordable care, which creates competition and the need for Advance to expand and enhance required services. In the coming months, as Medicaid guidelines change, we anticipate a spike in the number of uninsured and underinsured patients needing access to our services and programs. Our growing patient base will need to leverage the essential structure of our health center: SFDS (Sliding Fee Discount Schedule), same day access, and enabling services to ensure their wellbeing.

[TEXT] Workforce. Not only do we have a responsibility to hire and train the next generation of health care professionals, but we also have a responsibility to ensure workforce is deployed to areas of greatest need. In both counties that complete our service area there are multiple community reports of office and hospital closures that only increase the demand for qualified providers. In many cases we are creating strategies to support these practices via managed services to ensure quality and access are maintained in our community. The sustainability of primary care, especially in the rural designated parts of our service area, is essential. Advance is the measured and documented safety net for Wake and Franklin counties.

[TEXT] Reimbursement. As of Oct 1, 2025, Medicaid reimbursement across North Carolina was reduced by 3%. This policy will not change how we provide care, however; it will challenge our overall mission - less resources for patients that need access. Again, as the safety net for Wake and Franklin counites, thousands of years working families are depending on the ACH system to manage their care, support their health goals, and assist them in navigating an ever-changing health care landscape. Source(s): NC Medicaid Expansion implemented Dec 1, 2023 (NC DHHS Medicaid Bulletin #MA-2403).

[HEADING] 5. Describe how you will:

[TEXT] a. Conduct and update your needs assessment.

[TEXT] ACH conducts a comprehensive Community Health Needs Assessment (CHNA) at least once every three years and continuously monitors service area data to inform ongoing program planning, quality improvement, and resource allocation. ACH's needs assessment process is designed to identify emerging community health trends, assess access barriers, and align services with population health needs.

[TEXT] ACH met compliance standards during the 2024 Operational Site Visit (OSV). Per the 2024 OSV Review

[TEXT] Chapter 3 - Needs Assessment | Compliance Status: Met ACH adheres to Section 330(k)(2) and Section 330(k)(3)(J) of the Public Health Service (PHS) Act; and 42 CFR 51c.104(b) (2-3), 42 CFR 51c.303(k), 42 CFR 56.104(b)(2), 42 CFR 56.104(b)(4), and 42 CFR 56.303(k)

[TEXT] ACH actively contributes to countywide assessments, including the Wake County Community Health Needs Assessment (2025) and the Franklin County Community Health Assessment (2024), ensuring alignment between local and federal priorities. The ACH Comprehensive Community Needs Assessment incorporates both internal and external data sources, including:

[TEXT] . National and state data: Health Resources Service Administration/Bureau of Primary Health Care (HRSA/BPHC) Clinical Quality Measures; CDC; HHS Agency for Healthcare Research and Quality; Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System (BRFSS); SAMHSA National Survey on Drug Use and Health; and U.S. Census Bureau.

[TEXT] . Local and regional data: County Health Rankings; local hospital and social service utilization reports; and HPSA/MUA designations.

[TEXT] · Internal and program data: UDS reports and Health Center Program GeoCare Navigator analyses (poverty, income, insurance, demographics, race/ethnicity); patient satisfaction surveys; clinical Quality Improvement (QI) data; and provider productivity and utilization trends.

[TEXT] · Strategic inputs: ACH's Board-approved Strategic Plan, operational assessments, and environmental scans.

[TEXT] In addition to the triennial comprehensive assessment, ACH continuously evaluates patient feedback, community input, and real-time performance data to identify and respond to emerging needs. [TEXT] Findings directly inform strategic and operational planning, including service expansion, site development, workforce recruitment, and outreach priorities. Needs assessment data is also used to evaluate and adjust ACH's mix of in-scope and referral-based services, ensuring resources are directed toward the highest- priority community health needs.

[HEADING] b. Regularly update your Scope of Project in response to the needs for additional services.

[TEXT] ACH maintains a formal, structured process for monitoring community and patient needs and updating its HRSA-approved Scope of Project to ensure that services remain responsive, comprehensive, and compliant with federal requirements.

[TEXT] Each year, ACH conducts a detailed review of patient demographic, utilization, and outcome data, including UDS reports, local community health assessments, and feedback gathered from patients, providers, and staff, to identify emerging health trends, service gaps, and opportunities to expand or refine care delivery. When analysis indicates the need for additional services or delivery methods, ACH evaluates feasibility, financial impact, and alignment with organizational priorities, HRSA expectations, and the needs identified in the CHNA.

[TEXT] Proposed additions or modifications are reviewed by the Executive Leadership Team, Quality Improvement Committee, and Board of Trustees to ensure consistency with ACH's mission, strategic goals, and long- term sustainability. If a proposed change meets HRSA's definition of an in-scope addition, deletion, or modification, a formal Change in Scope (CIS) request is submitted for HRSA approval prior to implementation.

[TEXT] In addition to annual reviews, ACH continuously monitors new initiatives, grant-funded programs, and strategic partnerships that may necessitate adjustments to the approved Scope of Project. This ongoing process ensures that ACH's service mix, delivery sites, and modalities - including in-person, mobile, and telehealth services - remain aligned with evolving community needs and HRSA requirements.

[TEXT] By maintaining this proactive and systematic approach, ACH ensures that its Scope of Project accurately reflects the organization's capacity, supports equitable access to care, and advances the mission of Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[HEADING] c. Use patient and community input to inform and improve your service delivery.

[TEXT] ACH actively engages patients and community stakeholders to ensure that its services remain responsive to local needs and aligned with the populations it serves. Patient and community input is gathered through multiple structured channels, analyzed by leadership, and incorporated into ongoing planning, quality improvement, and service delivery decisions. Including but not limited to the following engagement:

[TEXT] . Patient Input. ACH's Board of Trustees, of which more than 51% are health center patients, plays a central role in representing the voice of the patient community. The Board provides ongoing oversight and guidance on policies, services, and access issues that impact patient experience and outcomes. In addition, ACH regularly conducts patient satisfaction surveys, focus groups, and post-visit feedback opportunities to capture patient perspectives on access, quality, communication, and cultural competence. Survey data are reviewed by site leadership and the Quality Improvement Committee to identify trends and implement corrective actions or enhancements.

[TEXT] · Community Input. ACH collaborates closely with community organizations, local health departments, school systems, housing agencies, and faith-based partners to assess needs and coordinate services. Input is also gathered through participation in community health assessments, regional coalitions, and stakeholder forums. These collaborations provide insight into emerging public health priorities, social drivers of health, and gaps in available community resources.

[TEXT] · Continuous Improvement. Findings from patient and community feedback are reviewed and integrated into ACH's Quality Improvement and Strategic Planning processes. This ensures that service enhancements - such as expanded hours, new programs, or additional enabling services - are directly informed by the voices of those served.

[TEXT] Through this structured approach, ACH ensures that patients and community members remain active partners in shaping accessible, high-quality, and culturally responsive care throughout the service area.

[TEXT] 1. Describe how the proposed service delivery sites on Form 5B: Service Sites will support access to your services (consistent with Form 5A: Services Provided) and minimize barriers within the proposed service area, including:

[TEXT] a. Where your service delivery sites are located, compared to where the target population lives and works.

[TEXT] ACH has strategically located its service delivery sites and mobile unit (Form 5B) to maximize accessibility for the target population and ensure full alignment with the scope of services provided (Form 5A). Each site is positioned in neighborhoods with the highest concentrations of medically underserved residents - areas characterized by high poverty rates, chronic disease burden, and limited access to private health care providers. Strategic locations include:

[TEXT] . Proximity to Patients' Homes and Workplaces: ACH sites are located in or near communities where most patients live and work, reducing transportation barriers and improving convenience for families and working adults.

[TEXT] · Accessible to Employment Centers and Schools: Several sites are situated near major employment corridors, schools, and public housing complexes, enabling patients to seek care without missing work or school.

[TEXT] . Urban and Rural Reach: ACH maintains a balanced network of urban and rural locations to serve both densely populated areas and remote communities. Rural sites reduce travel time for isolated residents, while urban clinics reach economically disadvantaged populations facing access challenges within the city. ACH has a mobile clinic that brings primary care, screenings, chronic care management, and other services directly to neighborhoods and schools, mitigating geographic and transportation barriers.

[HEADING] b. How you will address geographic barriers, location of sites, and hours of operation.

[TEXT] ACH is committed to ensuring that every resident of Wake and Franklin Counties has access to comprehensive, high-quality, and affordable care - regardless of geographic, transportation, or scheduling barriers. ACH continuously evaluates the service area in partnership with the North Carolina Community Health Center Association (NCCHCA), neighboring health centers, and community safety-net organizations to identify areas where primary care shortages and access gaps persist.

[TEXT] Addressing Geographic Barriers. ACH serves both densely populated urban neighborhoods and rural, medically underserved communities. Patients in Franklin County often face rural access challenges such as long travel distances, limited provider availability, and inadequate public transportation options. In contrast, patients in urban Wake County may encounter heavy traffic congestion, lack of reliable transit in certain neighborhoods, and difficulty obtaining care near their homes or workplaces. To address these issues, ACH collaborates with county agencies and local partners to provide transportation assistance, including ride-share or community transit vouchers. Care Coordinators assist patients in scheduling appointments and connecting to community-based transit programs, ensuring that transportation is never a barrier to receiving care.

[TEXT] Location of Sites. ACH has strategically located its clinical sites in medically underserved and high-need areas to maximize accessibility for the populations most in need. Sites are geographically distributed across both Wake and Franklin Counties to provide a balance of rural and urban access. The placement of sites aligns with population density, poverty concentrations, and health-disparity indicators identified through ongoing needs assessments. Expansion of service locations since the last SAC application, demonstrates ACH's intentional commitment to reducing travel times and aligning services with where patients live, work, and attend school. As shared above, ACH has the flexibility to respond to community needs with mobile medical, dental, and behavioral health.

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] Hours of Operation. To further enhance accessibility, ACH offers extended hours at key locations, including early morning, evening, and weekend appointments. Same-day appointments and dedicated urgent-care slots support patients with acute needs, while telehealth visits provide a convenient option for patients unable to travel to a clinic. For urgent concerns after regular business hours, ACH provides 24/7 access through its after-hours and on-call offerings, which connect patients to an on-call licensed provider via the professional answering service, ensuring continuity of care and timely clinical advice.

[TEXT] Through strategic site placement, extended hours, HIPAA-compliant telehealth with Epic integration, and robust enabling services, ACH effectively minimizes the impact of geographic and logistical barriers. These coordinated efforts ensure that all members of the target population - whether rural, urban, working, uninsured, or transportation-limited - can access timely, patient-centered care that supports equitable health outcomes across the region.

[TEXT] Collectively, these integrated strategies ensure that all patients within the service area can readily access ACH primary, dental, and behavioral health services without geographic or financial barriers.

[HEADING] REQUIRED SERVICES (Form 5A)

[TEXT] General Primary Medical Care - Column (1); Column (2)

[TEXT] ACH delivers comprehensive, age-inclusive primary care - prevention, acute and chronic management, patient education, referrals, and follow-up. Care is team-based and integrated with behavioral health, dental, pharmacy, and enabling services. Referrals are based on documented medical necessity and tracked in the EHR to ensure continuity (care transitions, discharge planning, results reconciliation).

[TEXT] · Column (2): Neighborhood Clinic - Urgent Care, Holly Springs (professional services agreement).

[TEXT] Diagnostic Laboratory - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH provides on-site laboratory services to support timely diagnosis and management of patient health needs. Medical assistants and nurses perform specimen collection, processing, and interpretation of results, and conduct Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments (CLIA)-waived and moderate- complexity laboratory tests appropriate for the treatment and management of common conditions within the patient population.

[TEXT] ACH performs a comprehensive range of in-office Point of Care Testing (POCT) to support timely clinical decision making and improve patient outcomes. Available POCT includes glucose, hemoglobin A1C, strep, influenza (flu), COVID-19, mononucleosis (mono), Helicobacter pylori (H. pylori), PT/INR, rapid bacterial vaginosis (BV), urine hCG (pregnancy test), urine dipstick, and respiratory syncytial virus (RSV).

[TEXT] · Column (3): LabCorp (discounted rates; write-offs for SFS-eligible patients).

[TEXT] Diagnostic Radiology - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH provides diagnostic radiology services that meet the program descriptor definition of processing and interpreting radiologic images to guide the provider's subsequent care and/or treatment of a patient. These services include, at minimum, plain medical films (X-rays) that assist clinicians in diagnosing and managing a wide range of medical conditions.

[TEXT] Diagnostic radiology will be provided directly by ACH at Advance Axcess and Franklin County CarePlex sites soon.

[TEXT] · Column (3): RightCare (formerly Project Access) for imaging (echo, MRI, CT, US, X-ray, PET/CT, B- read), at no cost to SFS-eligible patients.

[TEXT] Screenings - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH's providers and nursing staff deliver a full range of health screenings based on identified patient risk factors. Screenings include those for COVID-19, cancer, communicable diseases (including HIV, Hepatitis C, and other sexually transmitted infections), cholesterol, and blood lead levels. Cancer screenings include Pap tests, mammograms, and fecal immunochemical tests (FIT).

[TEXT] Coverage for Emergencies During and After Hours - Column (1); Column (2) ACH maintains written operating procedures to ensure an effective response to patient medical emergencies occurring after normal business hours. To provide continuous access to care, ACH utilizes an established system offering coverage 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. After-hours calls are routed to CareXM, a professional answering service, which records the patient's name and reason for the call and notifies the on-call provider as appropriate. The on-call provider triages calls, provides clinical guidance, and refers patients to the appropriate level of care, including the nearest emergency department when necessary. All encounters are documented in the EHR.

[TEXT] All ACH sites utilize an EHR system that allows on-call providers to securely access patient medical records and health histories from the clinic or remotely, enhancing care coordination and continuity. In addition, all ACH practitioners have access to external health information through Health Information Exchange (HIE) networks, including Care Everywhere and the Epic Admission, Discharge, and Transfer (ADT) interface, to ensure seamless integration of health services across care settings.

[TEXT] HIE network participants include WakeMed and UNC REX Hospital, which assists in coordination of care and follow-up. If an ACH patient is admitted other than through a referral, hospitalists notify ACH through the EHR. Nurse Care Managers employed by ACH are embedded on-site at partner hospitals and meet with ACH patients upon admission or discharge to coordinate post-hospital care. This includes scheduling follow-up visits and ensuring a smooth transition back to primary care.

[TEXT] Most ACH patients residing in Franklin County receive hospital services at WakeMed hospitals; however, some also utilize Duke Raleigh Hospital and UNC REX Hospital for inpatient or specialty care as needed.

[TEXT] . Column (2): CareXM - formerly Telemed. To ensure continuity of care, ACH has developed an on-call system and mechanisms for after-hours instruction through an After-Hours Answering Service. ACH patients utilize the service to contact their provider for "after hours" emergent care. ACH pays for this service monthly with no cost to patients. ACH reviews after-hours logs daily and documents all clinical dispositions and follow-up in the EHR.

[TEXT] Voluntary Family Planning - Column (1)

[TEXT] ACH provides comprehensive family planning services that promote reproductive health and support patients in making informed decisions about their care. Providers and clinical staff offer individualized counseling on available contraceptive and reproductive options, ensuring that patients receive education consistent with their values, preferences, and medical needs.

[TEXT] Clinical services include management, treatment, and procedures for a patient's chosen method of contraception - such as subdermal contraceptive implant placement, intrauterine device (IUD) insertion, and related follow-up care.

[HEADING] Immunizations - Column (1)

[TEXT] Well Child Services - Column (1)

[TEXT] ACH provides comprehensive well-child services delivered by physicians and advanced practice providers in a family practice setting. These services offer preventive care and treatment for newborns, infants, children, and adolescents to support healthy growth and development.

[TEXT] Services include regular and periodic physical examinations; growth and developmental assessments; age- appropriate screenings and tests (such as vision, hearing, oral health, and immunization status); laboratory testing as indicated; and preventive health education and counseling for children and families. Providers also review developmental milestones, nutrition, safety, and behavioral health concerns to promote early identification and intervention when needed.

[TEXT] Gynecology Care - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH provides comprehensive gynecological services delivered by physicians and advanced practice providers. Services include regular preventive assessments and appropriate treatment for women across the lifespan. Core services encompass pelvic and breast exams, cervical cancer screening, and the review of menstrual and reproductive history, gynecological symptoms, and basic gynecological ultrasounds to support early detection and management of reproductive health conditions.

[TEXT] Preventive counseling, contraceptive management, and referral for specialized care are also provided as appropriate.

[TEXT] Preventive Dental - Column (1)

[TEXT] ACH employs qualified dental staff who provide comprehensive preventive dental services to promote oral health and prevent disease. These services are provided via a 340B contractual agreement with medications supplied to patients at the 340B cost plus a nominal filling fee.

[TEXT] · Column (3): NC MedAssist is a statewide nonprofit pharmacy that provides prescription medications to eligible patients including uninsured, underinsured and homeless patients. ACH pays for membership to NC MedAssist. No cost to underinsured and uninsured patients.

[TEXT] This service is available to every ACH patient, including individuals served through the HCH program. Additionally, ACH addresses the needs of this population by utilizing grant funding to provide co-pay assistance to uninsured or underinsured patients who may not otherwise be able to pay for essential medications.

[TEXT] Health Care for the Homeless (HCH) Required Substance Use Disorder Services (SUD) - Column (1) ACH licensed clinical professionals rotate between sites to ensure consistent access to SUD services across the service area, including individuals served through the HCH program. Staff are trained and credentialed to provide SUD counseling under clinical supervision, and ACH maintains licensed supervisory staff to ensure quality, compliance, and adherence to best practices. Staff provide treatment for substance use disorders for clients - this includes screening, diagnosis, and treatment services for substance use disorders; harm/risk reduction and age-appropriate counseling to address identified risk factors; detoxification; and other individual and/or group treatment. This coordinated approach enables patients to receive timely, integrated treatment within the primary care setting and supports long-term recovery and wellness

[TEXT] Effective January 12, 2023, the Drug Enforcement Administration (DEA) and the Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration (SAMHSA) implemented the Medication Access and Training Expansion (MATE) Act as part of the Consolidated Appropriations Act of 2023. All DEA-registered prescribers must complete a one-time, eight-hour approved training on managing patients with opioid or other substance use disorders before applying for or renewing a DEA registration; this requirement may also be satisfied through previous completion of qualifying addiction-medicine training in medical or nursing school or prior DATA-Waiver training. ACH prescriber status includes:

[TEXT] . 2024-2025: Prescriber team includes Dr. Colin Ottey, MD; Dr. Ngozi Onoh, Psychiatric-Mental Health Nurse Practitioner (PMHNP); and Amber Rucker, Physician Assistant (PA).

[TEXT] . By November 2025: ACH will add two additional prescribers - Sadonna Cofield, Nurse Practitioner (NP), and Omotunde Adeyemi, Nurse Practitioner - bringing the total to five.

[TEXT] · Goal for 2026: Increase to six trained and authorized Medications for Opioid Use Disorder (MOUD) prescribers within ACH to ensure sustainability and expanded patient access.

[TEXT] ACH utilizes the standardized AUDIT-C and DAST tools to screen patients for substance use disorders. The results from the screening are documented in the EHR system, and patients who screen for risk are educated regarding their results by a Licensed Clinical Social Worker (LCSW) who is equipped to provide an immediate intervention per the Screening, Brief Intervention, and Referral to Treatment (SBIRT) model. The goal of this brief intervention is to move the client to a point of readiness to initiate appropriate treatment. Patients are then referred as needed to an onsite behavioral health provider. After the behavioral health visit, the behavioral health and primary care providers meet to review the plan of care. If an outside referral is needed, care management staff assist with making a referral, work to obtain results with the referral provider after the visit, and schedule any follow-up visits needed with ACH.

[TEXT] Primary care and behavioral health providers share the same EHR, share scheduling, and meet face-to- face to discuss complex needs of patients - for instance, when a patient has a debilitating medical condition such as cirrhosis, or when the behavioral health provider has sent the patient for more complex treatment such as detox or inpatient psychiatry. Providers are also able to alert each other and share notes via EHR.

[TEXT] ACH provides the required substance use disorder services for the homeless special population via dedicated substance use disorder staff, physicians, and advanced practice providers.

[TEXT] Case Management - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH employs designated care coordinators to provide case/care management services across all levels of care, ensuring a seamless continuum of care for patients throughout treatment and any needed referrals. Providers, Licensed Clinical Social Workers (LCSWs), Licensed Clinical Addiction Specialists (LCASs), clinical support staff, and registered dietitians actively participate in the care management process. This includes coordination of specialty and external referrals, hospital admissions, discharge planning, and patient tracking to promote continuity and quality of care.

[TEXT] LCSWs provide referrals for patients' mental health and substance use needs when these services cannot be met internally and collaborate with providers to develop comprehensive plans of care. The LCSW/LCAS provide clinical counseling for individuals experiencing homelessness, and also assists patients in obtaining needed community resources such as food, clothing, and shelter.

[TEXT] Following provider counseling regarding tests, treatment, and follow-up care, an LCSW reviews the information with each patient to ensure understanding of all instructions. When a referral is needed, whether between ACH sites or to an external specialty care provider - the LCSW or Behavioral Health Coordinator arranges the appointment, notifies the patient of the date and time, and transmits relevant chart information to the referral provider via secure fax. The LCSW then confirms receipt of the information and documents the referral in the EHR.

[TEXT] All referrals are entered and tracked through the EHR system. If a patient misses an appointment with a referral provider, staff contact the patient to determine the reason and assist in rescheduling. Patients receive reminders by phone, text message, and mail regarding appointment dates, times, and locations. When barriers to care arise, staff assist patients in addressing those barriers - such as arranging transportation - to ensure timely access to needed services.

[TEXT] · Column (3): RightCare - formerly Project Access. RightCare provides health care services to adults and children in Wake and Franklin Counties. SFS eligible patients can be referred to RightCare for case management services. Services are provided at no cost to the patient.

[TEXT] Eligibility Assistance - Column (1); Column (3)

[TEXT] ACH has trained staff who provide health insurance marketplace and other enrollment assistance year- round, with additional support added during the annual open enrollment period. As a Certified Application Counselor Designated Organization (CDO), ACH's outreach and enrollment staff educate patients on affordable insurance options, including available third-party coverage. Staff work with patients to determine eligibility for federal, state, and local assistance programs that support access to medical and enabling services. They also provide information to help patients make informed decisions about their coverage, including understanding potential out-of-pocket costs.

[TEXT] Enrollment staff assist patients throughout the entire enrollment process, connecting them with their selected coverage option(s) and ensuring that coverage is activated without delay. ACH has implemented process improvements to reflect provisions of the Affordable Care Act and supports enrollment in expanded health insurance coverage through the health insurance marketplace. These services are available to all ACH patients, including those served through the HCH program.

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] Health Education - Column (1)

[TEXT] ACH provides individualized health education during each patient encounter to promote self-management and healthy lifestyle choices. Education is delivered by physicians, advanced practice providers, licensed clinical social workers/addiction specialists (LCSW/LCAS), registered dietitians, and nursing staff at multiple points of care.

[TEXT] Through the EHR, patients receive education materials tailored to their specific health needs, language, and literacy level. In addition to in-clinic education, ACH participates in local health fairs and community events to provide information on healthy behaviors and preventive care. Registered dietitians also conduct group education sessions and healthy eating/cooking demonstrations at community outreach events to encourage nutrition awareness and disease prevention.

[TEXT] Dia-Beat It Program (Health Equity Partnership): ACH collaborates with the local YMCA through its community health equity partnership to offer Dia-Beat It, an eight-week diabetes prevention and management program. The program focuses on improving nutrition, increasing physical activity, and promoting overall wellness for adults at risk for or living with diabetes.

[TEXT] Under the coordination of ACH's health education and nutrition staff in partnership with YMCA program coordinators, participants receive group education sessions, individualized coaching, and practical tools to support healthy lifestyle changes. Core topics include meal planning, portion control, label reading, and strategies for maintaining long-term behavioral changes.

[TEXT] This initiative strengthens community partnerships and supports ACH's mission to reduce chronic disease disparities through prevention, education, and access to supportive resources.

[TEXT] Outreach - Column (1)

[TEXT] ACH employs Community Engagement Specialists who identify and recruit new patients while increasing community awareness of ACH's programs and services. The Community Engagement Department leads efforts in marketing and communications, outreach and enrollment, community health screenings, health education, voter registration, advocacy, and engagement with elected officials.

[TEXT] The department coordinates weekly events across Wake and Franklin Counties, tailoring outreach activities to meet the unique needs of local residents, including individuals experiencing homelessness. Through these efforts, ACH strengthens community partnerships, promotes access to care, and advances health equity by connecting residents with affordable, comprehensive health services.

[TEXT] ACH provides services to individuals experiencing homelessness at all clinical sites, ensuring equitable access to comprehensive care. Most homeless patients receive services at the Southeast Raleigh - South and Horizon at Oak City Cares locations. At Oak City Cares, ACH collaborates with multiple community partners co-located within the facility to expand access and coordinate care.

[TEXT] These sites emphasize outreach and provide integrated primary and behavioral health services, connecting individuals experiencing homelessness with essential medical, behavioral, and enabling services to support overall health and stability.

[TEXT] ACH extends access to care through mobile site visits at community locations, including the Women's Center, a local homeless shelter. Mobile teams provide on-site primary and preventive health services, focusing on individuals who experience barriers to traditional clinic access. Services include health assessments, screenings, immunizations, and linkage to ongoing medical, behavioral health, and enabling services.

[TEXT] These outreach efforts strengthen continuity of care, promote early intervention, and ensure that individuals experiencing homelessness - particularly women and families - receive accessible, compassionate, and comprehensive health services in familiar, community-based settings.

[TEXT] ACH enhances patient education and outreach through the It's Giving Health session, a monthly series led by the Health Educator. The series serves as a digital platform to promote preventive health, wellness, and disease management education in a relatable, accessible format. Each episode features health center providers, community partners, and patient voices discussing topics such as nutrition, mental health, chronic disease prevention, and health equity. By delivering culturally relevant content through a modern communication channel, ACH extends its health education efforts beyond the clinic, engaging both current and prospective patients across diverse communities. The session supports ACH's mission to improve health literacy, increase awareness of available services, and empower individuals to make informed decisions about their health.

[TEXT] Mental Health - Column (1)

Mental health services are available to all ACH patients, including individuals served through the HCH program.

[TEXT] ACH utilizes evidence-based screening tools such as the PHQ-2, PHQ-9, GAD-7, PCL-PTSD, and Bio- Physical Assessments to assess all patients for mental health needs, including depression and anxiety. Screening results are documented in the EHR, and patients who screen positive receive education and immediate brief intervention from an LCSW. When appropriate, the LCSW conducts additional assessments and provides intervention designed to move the patient toward readiness for ongoing treatment. As needed, patients are referred to an onsite behavioral health provider for continued care.

[TEXT] Following the behavioral health visit, behavioral health and primary care providers meet to review and update the patient's plan of care. If an external referral is required, care management staff coordinate the referral, track results, and schedule follow-up appointments to ensure continuity of care.

[TEXT] · Older Adults: Geriatric-focused care includes medication management, chronic condition monitoring, fall-risk assessment, preventive screenings, and coordination with home- and community-based service providers.

[TEXT] While most required and/or additional services are available at each site, specific services such as prenatal care, specialty care, or advanced imaging, ACH ensures access through formal referral relationships and coordinated follow-up. Referral and care coordination staff track appointments, obtain consultation results, and document outcomes in the Epic EHR to maintain continuity across providers.

[TEXT] ACH's sliding fee discount program and enabling services (eligibility assistance, transportation coordination, interpretation, and care management) remove financial, linguistic, and logistical barriers so that every patient, regardless of age, income, insurance status, or language, can access the full complement of required and additional services.

[TEXT] ACH is committed to delivering patient-centered care that recognizes each individual's unique needs, preferences, and circumstances. Care is not one-size-fits-all but instead designed in partnership with patients to empower them to take an active role in achieving their health goals.

[TEXT] . Tailored to the Individual: Providers and care teams use a whole-person approach that considers medical conditions, behavioral health needs, cultural background, language, and social drivers of health. Patients are engaged through shared decision-making, ensuring that treatment options align with their values, preferences, and life situations.

[TEXT] . Empowerment and Informed Decisions: ACH educates patients about their conditions, treatment options, and self-care strategies in clear, culturally appropriate language. Health educators, care managers, and care coordinators provide resources and coaching so that patients can make informed choices and confidently participate in their care.

[TEXT] · Comprehensive Care Plans: For patients with complex or chronic conditions, ACH's interdisciplinary care teams develop individualized care plans that integrate medical, behavioral, and enabling services. Each plan includes measurable clinical goals, patient-identified priorities, and timelines for follow-up. Patients and families actively participate in creating and revising their plans, reinforcing shared accountability, engagement, and continuity of care.

[TEXT] . Ongoing Support and Monitoring: ACH integrates care coordination, health coaching, and behavioral health consultation into primary care visits, ensuring that patients have continuous support. Progress is tracked through the EHR and quality dashboards, allowing care teams to adjust plans in real time and celebrate patient successes.

[TEXT] Through this model, ACH ensures that patients are not passive recipients of care but active partners in their health journey, supported by comprehensive care plans that help them meet their goals and improve their overall quality of life. Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] Project Narrative Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[TEXT] a. How you assess all patients for sliding fee discount eligibility based only on income and family size. See income definition in Chapter 9: Sliding Fee Discount Program of the Compliance Manual.

[TEXT] ACH provides services according to a Board-approved SFDP based solely on income and family size, consistent with Chapter 9 of HRSA's Compliance Manual. The SFDS applies to patients with incomes up to 200% of the FPG.

[TEXT] ACH utilizes written policies and procedures to implement the SFDS. These policies and procedures define income and family size, specify documentation or verification requirements for determining and recording family size and income, detail the specific structure for the SFDS itself, establish the frequency for re- evaluation of patient eligibility, and address provisions for waiving fees and nominal charges for specific patient circumstances.

[TEXT] Family size and income are verified using official documentation to determine wages and salary, excluding assets and other similar items, consistent with HRSA definitions. These figures are compared to the annually published FPG. ACH follows HRSA's definition of "family," which is a group of two or more persons related by birth, marriage, or adoption who live together; all such related persons are considered members of one family.

[TEXT] Eligibility determinations are conducted respectfully, confidentially, and in a culturally appropriate manner to avoid barriers to care. Acceptable income documentation includes recent pay stubs, tax returns, or other verifiable proof of earnings; assets are not considered.

[TEXT] When patients inquire about or are invited to apply for the Sliding Fee Discount Program, front-office staff or Patient Financial Navigators provide assistance with completing the application. Applications are reviewed and updated annually, or sooner if there is a change in household income or size. For patients who are unemployed, report zero income, or are homeless or transitioning from homelessness, eligibility is re-evaluated every six months to ensure continued accuracy.

[TEXT] Patients without income documentation may self-declare income for one visit per year; documentation must be provided at the next visit or the patient is classified as self-pay.

[TEXT] For homeless individuals, ACH follows Section 330 of the Public Health Service Act (42 U.S.C. § 254b) and Bureau of Primary Health Care definitions of homelessness. Per guidance, an individual may be considered homeless if they are "doubled up" with others, or if they are a previously homeless person being discharged from a hospital, prison, or similar institution without stable housing to return to. All patients who identify as homeless, regardless of insurance status, must provide documentation of their homeless status consistent with this definition. Acceptable documentation includes a certification letter from a shelter or social service agency or correlating verification forms such as household instability or "doubled-up" documentation. This documentation is attached to the patient's SFDP application to ensure eligibility determination aligns with HRSA requirements.

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] ACH's Practice Management System calculates the percentage of FPG based on income and family size and flags records for review. Eligibility is re-verified annually, and the Chief Financial Officer and Practice Managers audit files to ensure accuracy and adherence to policy.

[TEXT] Reference Attachment 10: Sliding Fee Discount Schedule(s).

[TEXT] b. How you adjust patient charges based on the ability to pay (consistent with Attachment 10: Sliding Fee Discount Schedule).

[TEXT] ACH adjusts patient charges based on ability to pay through its Board-approved SFDP. Discounts are applied using a SFDS aligned with the most recent FPG and determined by verified household income and family size.

[TEXT] The SFDP applies to all individuals and families with annual incomes between 100% and 200% of the FPG. Discounts (flat or percentage-based) are applied consistently across all service types, including medical, behavioral health, dental, nursing, nutrition, pharmacy, urgent care, integrated care, and OB/GYN.

[TEXT] Patients with annual incomes at or below 100% of the FPG are charged only a nominal fee, while those between 101% and 200% of the FPG receive graduated discounts. The SFDS includes four pay classes above 100% FPG - 101-125%, 126-150%, 151-175%, and 176-200%. No sliding fee discount is approved for individuals or families with incomes exceeding 200% of the FPG.

[TEXT] All services are billed at their full established charge, and discounts are applied according to each patient's verified eligibility level. Uninsured patients and those who are underinsured (with self-pay balances such as co-payments or deductibles) are encouraged to apply for the SFDP.

[TEXT] Eligibility is determined and documented annually, based on verification of income and household size, and reassessed whenever a change in financial circumstances occurs. ACH ensures that no patient is denied care due to inability to pay, thereby maintaining equitable access to all health center services.

[TEXT] Each year, the Board of Trustees, comprised of a patient-majority membership, reviews and approves the SFDS to incorporate the most recent FPG. As part of this review, the Board evaluates the structure and effectiveness of the discount schedule to ensure it continues to reduce financial barriers to care. This includes reviewing UDS data, practice management system financial reports, and patient satisfaction survey results to assess whether patients across all discount pay classes are accessing care.

[TEXT] In conjunction with this annual review, ACH's policies and procedures governing implementation of the sliding fee scale are also reviewed and updated as needed to ensure continued compliance with HRSA's Sliding Fee Discount Program requirements.

[TEXT] d. How you evaluate your sliding fee discount program to ensure that it reduces financial barriers to care.

[TEXT] ACH regularly evaluates its SFDP to ensure it effectively reduces financial barriers and promotes equitable access to care.

[TEXT] The nominal and discount fee schedules are reviewed annually by the Board of Trustees to ensure continued affordability and alignment with the most current FPG. As part of this review, ACH analyzes utilization data, patient satisfaction survey results, and feedback from front-line staff and Patient Financial Navigators to assess whether fees remain reasonable and non-restrictive for low-income patients.

[TEXT] To further prevent financial hardship, ACH works directly with patients to establish payment plans when needed. In cases where nominal fees pose a financial burden, waivers or alternative arrangements may be granted. Waiver authority is delegated to the Chief Executive Officer, Chief Financial Officer, Chief Operating Officer, Chief Medical Officer, and Director of Patient Financial Services, with requests initiated by practice managers or providers.

[TEXT] ACH also monitors self-pay and uninsured visit trends, missed appointment rates, and collections data as part of its QI monitoring process. These findings are presented to the Board of Trustees during the annual SFDS review for consideration of any adjustments to fee structures or pay classes. Modifications are made as needed to ensure the SFDP continues to reduce financial barriers, maintain affordability, and support equitable access to all health center services.
