[TEXT] 7. Describe your process to ensure continuity of care for patients. Include:

[TEXT] a. Communication tools, referral processes, and electronic exchange of patient health records.

[TEXT] b. Hospital admitting privileges.

[TEXT] c. Receipt, follow-up, and recording of medical information from referral sources.

[TEXT] d. Follow-up for patients who are hospitalized or visit a hospital's emergency department.

[TEXT] ACH ensures continuity of care through well-defined communication systems, referral processes, electronic data exchange, and coordinated follow-up for patients receiving services both within and outside the health center network. ACH utilizes the Epic EHR system, which includes the Care Everywhere interoperability feature to securely exchange patient health information with external partners - such as hospitals, specialists, and other health care providers. Referral orders and care coordination activities are documented in the EHR to ensure providers have timely access to patient records and care plans. Referral staff coordinate and track external referrals to ensure receipt of consultation notes and test results, and the Care Management Department reviews all referrals to ensure follow-up is completed in accordance with care plans. Data sharing occurs securely through the NC Health Information Exchange (NCHIE) and integrated hospital portals. Communication tools such as direct messaging, patient portal communication, and phone follow-ups support timely coordination with patients and external partners.

[TEXT] ACH providers collaborate closely with hospital partners to ensure continuity of care but do not maintain direct admitting privileges. Instead, ACH maintains formal referral and communication protocols with area hospitals to facilitate inpatient coordination, data sharing, and post-discharge transitions. Hospitalists and emergency department physicians provide inpatient care, while ACH providers resume primary care management upon discharge. Continuity of care following hospitalization or emergency department use is a key quality focus. Providers document all hospital and emergency referrals in Epic, including the receiving facility, reason for transfer, and diagnosis. The Care Management team accesses hospital discharge data daily, contacts patients, reviews discharge instructions, reconciles medications, and schedules follow-up visits within seven days post-discharge.

[TEXT] HIE network participants include WakeMed and UNC REX Hospital, which assists in coordination of care and follow-up. If an ACH patient is admitted other than through a referral, hospitalists notify ACH through the EHR. Nurse Care Managers employed by ACH are embedded on-site at partner hospitals and meet with ACH patients upon admission or discharge to coordinate post-hospital care. This includes scheduling follow-up visits and ensuring a smooth transition back to primary care.

[TEXT] For after-hours emergencies, ACH's 24-hour on-call system ensures patients have immediate access to a licensed provider for triage and referral to appropriate care. During clinic hours, medical emergencies are managed by the Medical Emergencies and Emergency Transport Policy until EMS arrives.

[TEXT] In accordance with ACH's Hospitalization Tracking Policy, all hospitalizations and emergency department visits (excluding behavioral health) are tracked through the EHR. When notified of a hospitalization or emergency department visit, clinical staff log into the EpicCare Everywhere admission and discharge portal to import discharge summaries into the EHR, while the Care Management Department contacts the patient to schedule a follow-up appointment within seven days. Care Managers review discharge records, conduct medication reconciliation, update care plans, and ensure appropriate Care Management enrollment. ACH staff make three outreach attempts within a seven-day period using at least two methods, including telephone, mail, chart messaging, email, or fax. If the patient cannot be reached, a letter is sent, and ACH uses best efforts and available resources to locate and engage the patient, including pharmacy and hospital outreach, family contact, and searches through NCHIE.

[TEXT] To ensure HRSA compliance, ACH tracks hospitalization follow-up appointments monthly. Results of continuity-of-care metrics (hospital follow-up within seven days, closed referral rates, and 30-day readmission rates) are reported quarterly to the QI/QA Committee and incorporated into ACH's UDS performance reviews. The Data Analyst and site Practice Managers perform regular audits submitted to the Risk Manager and/or Compliance Officer to monitor adherence and outcomes. All follow-up activities, patient contacts, and external reports are documented in the EHR to ensure seamless coordination across care settings. Monitoring and data reporting are conducted under ACH's Program Monitoring and Data Systems Policy to ensure accurate, timely analysis of service utilization and performance trends, reinforcing ACH's commitment to continuous quality improvement and comprehensive, coordinated patient care.

These relationships ensure that services remain responsive to evolving community needs and that interventions are tailored to populations most at risk.

Collaborations go beyond day-to-day coordination to include joint planning, data sharing, and co-design of initiatives that improve community outcomes - supporting continuity of care, access to services not available on-site, and reduced non-urgent use of hospital emergency departments.

[TEXT] Existing Health Center Programs and Look-Alikes.

[TEXT] One FQHC Look-Alike operates in the service area: NeighborHealth Center, based in Raleigh, NC. NeighborHealth provides comprehensive primary and preventive care services, including family medicine, internal medicine, pediatrics, women's health, behavioral health, and chronic disease management. The organization also offers immunizations, laboratory services, care coordination, and limited dental and pharmacy assistance through partnerships. Services are available to patients regardless of ability to pay, with a sliding fee discount program based on income and family size.

[TEXT] In 2024, NeighborHealth served 7,885 total patients. The organization did not provide services to individuals experiencing homelessness or to migratory or seasonal agricultural workers and their family members. Source(s): UDS 2024.

[TEXT] ACH maintains a Memorandum of Agreement with NeighborHealth through which ACH provides dental services to NeighborHealth Center patients. This collaboration enhances continuity of care among community providers and expands access to comprehensive oral health services for the local population.

[TEXT] Several FQHCs are dominant in parts of the broader region but have no physical sites within the defined service area, including Carolina Family Health Centers, Lincoln Community Health Center, and CommWell Health (formerly Tri-County Community Health Council). These organizations operate in adjacent counties and extend some services to patients who may reside within the proposed service area. ACH and CommWell Health collaborate through the NCCHCA, supporting continuity of care, shared learning, and alignment of best practices across community providers.

[TEXT] The North Carolina Office of Rural Health (NCORH) - Farmworker Health Program administrative center is also based in Raleigh; however, this site does not provide direct services to the target population. Instead, NCORH contracts with health entities across the state that are located in areas with a high concentration of migratory and seasonal agricultural workers to deliver care to that population. ACH provides primary care services for farmworkers by referral from NCORH as needed, ensuring access to care for this vulnerable group within the service area.

[TEXT] ACH collaborates closely with the WakeMed system to support patient care coordination, including admissions, discharge planning, and follow-up. ACH maintains formal agreements with WakeMed for emergency medical services and hospitalist in-patient care for ACH patients.

[TEXT] These collaborative arrangements strengthen continuity of care, improve patient access to hospital-based and specialty services not available at ACH, and reduce the non-urgent use of hospital emergency departments.

[TEXT] Duke Health operates Duke Raleigh Hospital, a 204-bed facility located in Raleigh. The hospital provides a full range of services including cancer care, cardiovascular care, neuroscience, advanced gastrointestinal care, and wound healing. Duke Raleigh Hospital also maintains laboratory and imaging services, a pain clinic, 24/7 emergency care, community outreach, and education programs.

[TEXT] Through the RightCare (formerly Project Access) agreement, ACH collaborates with Duke Raleigh Hospital to support patient care, admissions, discharge planning, and follow-up. These arrangements enhance continuity of care across community providers, expand access to specialty services not available at ACH, and help reduce inappropriate emergency department utilization.

[TEXT] UNC REX Hospital, located in Raleigh and owned by the University of North Carolina Health Care System, also partners with ACH through the RightCare agreement to support patient care, admissions, discharge planning, and follow-up. In addition, UNC REX provides mobile mammography screenings for ACH patients. These collaborations collectively strengthen continuity of care across community providers, increase access to diagnostic and specialty services not available at ACH, and reduce non-urgent use of hospital emergency departments.

[TEXT] Organizational Structure. ACH operates as an independent, private, nonprofit corporation with Section 501(c)(3) status under a HCP model. The organizational structure is designed to ensure effective governance, clinical oversight, and administrative management while maintaining compliance with all HRSA Health Center Program requirements. Legal authority for the organization rests solely with the ACH Board of Trustees, which holds ultimate responsibility for all corporate policies, strategic direction, and oversight of operations.

[TEXT] Established in 1972, ACH receives funding under Section 330(e) as a Community Health Center and Section 330(h) as a Health Care for the Homeless Program. Over more than five decades, ACH has evolved into a leading patient-centered medical home recognized for providing high-quality, comprehensive primary care, dental, behavioral health, and enabling services to underserved, uninsured, and underinsured populations throughout its service area.

[TEXT] Board and Executive Relationship. The Board of Trustees exercises full authority consistent with HRSA Compliance Manual Chapter 19 requirements. The Board of Trustees appoints, evaluates, and - if necessary - dismisses the CEO, delegating day-to-day operational authority while retaining responsibility for policy setting, strategic direction, and budget approval. [TEXT] 5. Your experience and plans for maintaining continuity of services and responding to urgent primary health care needs during natural or man-made disasters and public health emergencies. Your response should be consistent with all applicable Federal, state, and local laws and regulations.

[TEXT] Cybersecurity and Data Protection. ACH maintains a comprehensive cybersecurity framework modeled after the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) Cybersecurity Framework and compliant with the HIPAA Security Rule. Policies and procedures are in place to protect HHS systems and data, including multi-factor authentication, encrypted data transmission and storage, continuous network monitoring, and an established incident response plan.

[TEXT] ACH regularly reviews and updates its cybersecurity program to address emerging threats and ensure ongoing compliance with HRSA and HHS requirements. All systems supporting the Health Center Program award, including electronic health records, financial systems, and reporting platforms, are secured within this framework to safeguard patient information and ensure uninterrupted service delivery.

[TEXT] Preparation, Response, and Recovery Plans. ACH has an Emergency Preparedness and Management Plan that addresses natural or manmade disasters, as well as emergent or established public health emergencies. This plan addresses the four phases of disasters, including mitigation, preparedness, response, and recovery. ACH strives to keep facilities open during the event of a disaster in order to respond to urgent primary health care needs. In the event that the health center is forced to close or experiences a total loss of facility capacity, the Emergency Preparedness and Management Plan incorporates procedures to connect patients with alternatives for primary care. ACH's Southeast Raleigh - South site has a generator, and the mobile unit can be deployed to provide services as needed.

[TEXT] Backup Systems to Facilitate Communications. ACH utilizes state-issued VIPER phones and most ACH employees have cell phones to communicate in the event of loss of land-line capability.

[TEXT] Patient Records Access. All patient records are maintained using the health center EHR system, which can be accessed via web connection (cell phone, iPad, laptop computer, etc.). The EHR system also has redundant off-site servers back up to guard against loss of information.

[TEXT] Integration into State and Local Preparedness Plans. The Emergency Preparedness and Management Plan is integrated into state and local preparedness plans, and ACH participates in planned emergency drills on the state and local level. This provides opportunities for ACH to coordinate with other systems of care to provide an integrated emergency response. The role of ACH is determined by the State of North Carolina based on the nature and type of emergency. ACH is also a key participant in the Capital Regional Access Committee (CAPRAC), which facilitates the development, implementation, and operation of a comprehensive regional patient care system based on accepted standards of care in the event of a natural or man-made disaster.

[HEADING] c. Diabetes and hypertension control.

[TEXT] ACH strives to decrease the percentage of patients 18-74 years of age with diabetes who had HbA1c levels greater than 9% (NOT under control). HbA1c >9% is an indicator of poor diabetes control, with a lower percentage representing better performance.

[TEXT] From 2020 through 2024, the percentage of patients diagnosed with diabetes has remained relatively stable overall, with modest year-to-year variation. In 2020, 25.40% of patients were identified as having diabetes, with a slight decline in 2021 (25.17%) and a subsequent rise to 28.23% in 2022. The percentage decreased to 23.82% in 2023, followed by an increase to 27.24% in 2024.

[TEXT] The number of diabetes patients followed a similar trend, ranging from 3,075 in 2020 to 3,339 in 2022, then decreasing to 2,975 in 2023 before climbing again to 3,084 in 2024. These shifts are influenced by factors such as patient turnover, expanded screening efforts, and improved diagnostic coding accuracy following the COVID-19 pandemic.

[TEXT] In response, ACH has continued to enhance its chronic disease management approach for patients with diabetes through expanded access to nutritional counseling, care coordination, medication management, and integrated behavioral health support. The center also leverages evidence-based tools and population health reports within the EHR to proactively identify patients with uncontrolled diabetes and engage them in follow-up care. Continued efforts are focused on improving HbA1c control rates and reducing diabetes- related complications across the patient population.

[TEXT] Comprehensive Diabetes Prevention and Education

[TEXT] Preventive health education, nutrition services, and chronic disease management are core components of ACH's patient-centered care model. Registered dietitians and nutritionists provide individualized counseling for patients managing diabetes, hypertension, and obesity, while group education sessions-known as Power Hours - offer interactive instruction on healthy eating, exercise, and lifestyle modification.

[TEXT] ACH promotes diabetes prevention and early detection through routine weight screenings for adults and children, annual bloodwork (including a comprehensive metabolic panel) for all overweight or obese patients, and same-day HbA1c testing for individuals with a family history or elevated risk factors. Patients receive tailored education on diabetes risk factors, prevention, and self-management through both individual and group sessions.

[TEXT] Health Educators conduct ongoing classes and workshops on chronic disease prevention and management. To address social drivers of health, ACH partners with Interfaith Food Shuttle to provide monthly fresh-food distributions at all sites, ensuring access to nutritious foods for patients and community

[TEXT] members. These integrated strategies improve health outcomes, strengthen community engagement, and reduce health disparities among the low-income populations served by ACH.

[TEXT] Diabetes: Hemoglobin A1c Poor Control (HbA1c > 9%). Diabetes control rates demonstrated variability during the 2020-2024 period, influenced in part by pandemic disruptions and care access challenges. In 2020, 43.12% of diabetic patients had poorly controlled HbA1c or no test documented. This percentage fluctuated between 25.76% and 27.43% in 2022-2023 before rising again to 44.23% in 2024. The number of patients with poor control mirrored these trends, from 1,326 in 2020 to 1,364 in 2024.

[TEXT] The 2024 increase likely reflects both improved screening and inclusion of new patients reestablishing care post-pandemic. In response, the health center has intensified its diabetes management efforts through point-of-care HbA1c testing, expanded access to registered dietitian, enhanced medication adherence programs, and team-based care that includes behavioral health support for lifestyle modification. The clinical leadership team continues to monitor diabetic control closely, with an emphasis on reducing the proportion of patients with HbA1c > 9% through coordinated care plans and continuous quality improvement initiatives.

[TEXT] Controlling High Blood Pressure (BP < 140/90 mmHg). Between 2020 and 2024, the percentage of patients diagnosed with hypertension within the health center's patient population demonstrated some fluctuation but remained a significant focus area for chronic disease management. In 2020, nearly half (49.92%) of medical patients presented with hypertension. This proportion gradually declined through 2023, reaching a low of 40.02%, before increasing again to 46.19% in 2024.

[TEXT] The total number of hypertension patients decreased from 6,344 in 2020 to 5,236 in 2023, followed by a modest increase to 5,464 in 2024. These changes may reflect several concurrent factors, including population shifts during the COVID-19 pandemic, enhanced screening and documentation processes, and expanded access to preventive and primary care services in subsequent years.

[TEXT] In response to these trends, the health center has strengthened its chronic disease management program through improved care coordination, the use of evidence-based treatment protocols, and proactive patient engagement strategies such as follow-up calls, home blood pressure monitoring, and nutrition education. Continued emphasis on hypertension control remains a clinical quality priority, with a focus on reducing complications and improving overall cardiovascular health among the patient population.

[TEXT] Between 2020 and 2024, the health center achieved a steady and significant improvement in hypertension control rates. In 2020, only 42.23% of patients with hypertension had controlled blood pressure. This measure increased each year, reaching 62.17% in 2024 - a 20-percentage point improvement over five years. The number of hypertensive patients with controlled blood pressure also grew from 2,679 in 2020 to 3,397 in 2024, reflecting enhanced chronic disease management and patient engagement.

[TEXT] This sustained progress is attributed to the implementation of evidence-based hypertension protocols, proactive outreach by care coordinators, improved medication adherence through pharmacy collaboration, and expanded access to home BP monitoring. Additionally, the use of EHR-based alerts and population health dashboards allowed care teams to identify and intervene with patients whose blood pressure readings were trending upward.

[HEADING] d. Screening for depression and follow-up planning, including depression remission.

[TEXT] ACH supports a fully integrated model of primary and behavioral health care, wherein patients receive behavioral health screenings, appropriate referral to treatment, and ongoing support for the collaborative plan of care by medical providers. ACH uses the PHQ-2 or PHQ-9, GAD-7, PCL-PTSD, and Bio-Physical Assessments to screen patients for depression at intake. Staff enter results in the EHR, which are reviewed by the provider with referral for in-house or outside behavioral health services as indicated. Patients may be reluctant to complete depression screening or may not be truthful in responses due to the impact of stigma regarding mental health conditions. Providers will educate the patient regarding the benefits of screening and the health center's commitment to confidentiality.

[TEXT] Depression Screening and Follow-Up Plan. From 2020 through 2024, the health center demonstrated consistent improvement in screening for depression and ensuring follow-up plans for patients with positive results. In 2020, 71.00% of patients were screened and had a documented follow-up plan when indicated. Despite a temporary decline in 2021 (57.28%), reflecting the operational disruptions associated with the COVID-19 pandemic, performance rebounded in subsequent years, rising steadily to 74.94% in 2024. The number of patients screened increased significantly from 8,259 in 2020 to 11,513 in 2024, underscoring the center's success in integrating behavioral health services into primary care workflows.

[TEXT] Behavioral health needs have increased sharply, particularly among adolescents and working-age adults. In response, ACH has expanded its integrated behavioral health model, embedding licensed clinicians within primary care teams to provide same-day consultations, brief therapy, and medication management. This co-located approach enhances early identification of behavioral health concerns and reduces stigma and delays in treatment.

[TEXT] This improvement is attributed to the implementation of standardized screening tools (PHQ-2 and PHQ-9) within the EHR, provider training on behavioral health integration, and the availability of LCSWs across all service sites. The center also strengthened its referral pathways and documentation practices to ensure timely follow-up for patients with positive screens, particularly within the Health Care for the Homeless and high-risk populations.

[TEXT] Depression Remission at Twelve Months. While year-to-year performance in depression remission varied, the data reflect ongoing progress toward achieving long-term behavioral health outcomes. After establishing baseline reporting in 2021 (11.05%), remission rates increased to 16.24% in 2023 before moderating to 10.04% in 2024. [TEXT] People experiencing homelessness often face significant barriers to accessing behavioral health services, including the absence of family or social support networks that can assist them in seeking or maintaining care. Through this integrated approach, ACH ensures that vulnerable populations, particularly those experiencing homelessness, receive coordinated, patient- centered behavioral health services designed to promote stability, recovery, and improved quality of life.

[HEADING] e. Tobacco use screening and cessation intervention.

[TEXT] Tobacco use screening and cessation intervention. From 2020 through 2024, ACH consistently maintained high performance in screening adult patients for tobacco use and providing cessation interventions when indicated. In 2020, 96.15% of patients aged 12 and older were screened and counseled on tobacco use. Although there was a temporary decline in 2021 (82.62%) - largely due to pandemic- related disruptions and reduced in-person visits - performance steadily improved in the following years, reaching 91.52% in 2024.

[TEXT] The total number of adult medical patients screened increased from 7,522 in 2020 to 9,733 in 2024, reflecting ACH's renewed focus on preventive health measures and robust documentation practices. The health center's providers integrate tobacco screening and cessation counseling into routine visits using standardized EHR prompts and evidence-based counseling protocols. Patients identified as tobacco users are offered immediate cessation support, including behavioral counseling, nicotine replacement therapy, and referral to the North Carolina Quitline.

[TEXT] f. Weight assessment and counseling for nutrition and physical activity for children and adolescents.

[TEXT] Weight Assessment and Counseling for Nutrition and Physical Activity (Children and Adolescents, Ages 3-17). Between 2020 and 2024, ACH observed a gradual decline in the percentage of pediatric patients receiving weight assessment and counseling for nutrition and physical activity. In 2020, 79.32% of children and adolescents were assessed and counseled, compared to 51.94% in 2024. The number of patients receiving this service varied over the five-year period, peaking at 2,653 in 2023.

[TEXT] This downward trend corresponds to several contributing factors, including the reduced frequency of in- person well-child visits during the pandemic and challenges in documenting counseling within the EHR. In response, ACH has implemented strategies to improve performance, including reinforcing documentation protocols, integrating nutrition and physical activity counseling prompts into visit templates, and expanding collaboration with registered dietitians and school-based health partners. These actions are designed to reestablish strong performance levels and promote early prevention of obesity and related chronic conditions among pediatric patients.

[TEXT] ACH will improve clinical quality and health outcomes by:

[TEXT] · Routine Documentation: Record height, weight, and BMI percentile for all patients ages 3 to 17 at each well-child and acute care visit.

[TEXT] · Preventive Counseling: Provide age-appropriate counseling on nutrition and physical activity for children and their caregivers, documented within the EMR.

[TEXT] . Ensure appropriate laboratory testing and referral to Nutrition and Behavioral health for children and adolescents who are underweight/overweight.

[TEXT] ACH will continue to advance clinical quality and health outcomes by implementing evidence-based practices, strengthening care coordination, and focusing on prevention, early detection, and effective management of chronic and behavioral health conditions.

[TEXT] 1. Describe how your governing board reflects the community you serve and how board members engage with patients to ensure that the health center is responsive to patient needs. Reference Form 6A: Current Board Member Characteristics.

[TEXT] The ACH Board of Trustees is structured in full compliance with Section 330 of the Public Health Service Act and HRSA Health Center Program requirements, ensuring it reflects and represents the community served.

[TEXT] ACH met compliance standards during the 2024 Operational Site Visit. Per the 2024 Operational Site Visit Review Chapter 20: Board Composition | Compliance Status - Met ACH adheres to Section 330(k)(3)(H) of the PHS Act; and 42 CFR 51c.304 and 42 CFR 56.304.

[TEXT] As documented in Form 6A: Current Board Member Characteristics, a majority of ACH's board members are active patients of the health center - at least 51% as required by HRSA. Collectively, the Board mirrors the demographic, cultural, and socioeconomic composition of the service area, with diversity in race, ethnicity, gender, age, income levels, and professional backgrounds. This alignment ensures that governance decisions are informed by the lived experiences, perspectives, and needs of the populations identified in the most recent CHNA, thereby strengthening accountability and responsiveness to the communities ACH serves.

[TEXT] The ACH Board of Trustees consists of twelve (12) members, seven (7) of whom are active users of ACH's services. The Board collectively represents a broad range of expertise, including disabilities advocacy, human resources, clinical research, higher education, consulting, training and development, government relations, finance, social work, human services, law, and homeless engagement (Health Care for the Homeless Special Population Representative). Of the twelve members, four (4) are male and eight (8) are female. Ethnicity includes one (1) Hispanic or Latino and eleven (11) Non-Hispanic or Latino; race includes nine (9) Black/African American, two (2) White/Caucasian, and one (1) identifying as more than one race. Only one (1) member (8%) receives greater than ten percent (10%) of income from the health care industry, preserving board independence.

[TEXT] No employee (including CEO) serves as a voting board member; the CEO is a non-voting ex-officio. Board members complete annual conflict of interest attestations and recuse as required. The board includes a designated HCH consumer representative to ensure governance decisions reflect the needs of people experiencing homelessness.

[TEXT] To ensure responsiveness to patient and community needs, Board members engage actively with the health center beyond their governance role, including but not limited to the following:

[TEXT] · Patient Advisory Input: Regular reports from patient satisfaction surveys, focus groups, and community listening sessions are presented to the Board and used to guide decisions on access, quality improvement, and service expansion.

[TEXT] · Direct Engagement: As active patients, many Board members provide continuous informal feedback on their care experiences, influencing operational decisions such as extended hours, telehealth enhancements, and mobile service delivery.

[HEADING] ADVANCE COMMUNITY HEALTH, INC. Non-Profit 501(c)(3) Corporation

[TEXT] The Mission of Advance Community Health Inc. (the "Corporation") is to deliver quality, compassionate primary healthcare - every patient, every time - in response to the needs of our communities. The Corporation provides services primarily to residents of Wake and Franklin counties; however, the Corporation cares for all, regardless of insurance status or ability to pay.

[HEADING] ARTICLE I. OFFICES

[TEXT] The Corporation may have such offices as the Board of Trustees may determine or as the affairs of the Corporation may require from time to time.

[HEADING] ARTICLE II. BOARD OF TRUSTEES

[TEXT] Section 1. General Powers. The Corporation is organized pursuant to North Carolina General Statutes, Chapter 55A (Nonprofit Corporation Act), and the affairs of the Corporation shall be managed by the Board of Trustees. The Board of Trustees shall, always, ensure that the Corporation operates in compliance with the laws of the State of North Carolina and with the federal rules and regulations that govern the funding and operation of community health centers. The Board of Trustees shall always reserve full authority. No individual, entity or committee, at any time, has approval or veto authority over the Board. The Board of Trustees shall operate in concert with the organization's fiscal year (April 1 - March 31).

[TEXT] Section 2. Number and Qualifications. The Corporation shall have two categories of Trustees, "patients" and "non-patients." The definition of "patient" includes any person (or their parent/legal guardian) who has utilized the Corporation as their principal source of primary or dental care within the last two years. A non-patient shall be defined as a representative of the community in the Corporation's service area.

[TEXT] The Board of Trustees shall be a self-perpetuating body with vacancies being filled by a majority vote of the members present at a duly constituted meeting of the Board of Trustees. At least fifty- one percent (51%) of board members shall be patients who shall be representative of the Corporation's patient demographics in terms of age, race, ethnicity and gender. The patient board members shall be representative of the various practice locations and communities served and shall be selected in keeping with federal rules and regulations that govern the funding and administration of healthcare centers. The Corporation receives special population funding, and at a minimum there shall be at least one Board member who represents persons who are experiencing homelessness.

[TEXT] The remaining members of the Board of Trustees shall be non-patients who, generally selected for their expertise, shall also be selected in keeping with the federal rules and regulations that govern the funding and administration of healthcare centers. The Corporation shall, always, strive to

[TEXT] Board Bylaws

[TEXT] Approved 06/24/2024

[TEXT] Page 2

[TEXT] Funding Opportunity Number: HRSA-26-004 Received Date: 11/5/2025 1:57:03 PM



========== PAGE 110 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242744

[TEXT] Grant Number: 6 H80CS00087-24-05

[TEXT] maintain balance between patients and non-patients Trustees, making every effort to achieve 49% non-patient representation on the board. No more than fifty percent (50%) of the non-patient Trustees may be individuals who derive greater than 10% of their annual income from the healthcare industry. Specifically, "individuals who derive their income from the healthcare industry" are defined as persons currently employed in organizations who provide primary healthcare, specialty services, hospital or rehabilitative services, including solo or private practice. The definition does not include persons retired from those organizations. Non-patient board members shall live or work in the Corporation's service area.

[TEXT] The number of Trustees shall be at least nine (9) and no more than seventeen (17) except when it becomes necessary or desirable to increase the size of the Board to accommodate additional practice sites, communities or expertise. In such case, the Corporation shall increase the size of the Board by no greater than two (2) additional members, one seat being designated for a patient and one for a non-patient. At no time shall the number of Trustees be greater than twenty-five (25).

[TEXT] No member of the Board of Trustees shall be a contractor of the organization. No member of the Board of Trustees shall be an employee of the Corporation, or be related by blood, marriage, or adoption to an employee of the Corporation. The definition of "relative" for purposes of the Board of Trustees includes spouse, parents, children, siblings, aunts, uncles, grandparents, domestic partners, or persons in these roles through adoption or marriage. Board members shall not use their position for preferential treatment for themselves, relatives, or close associates.

[TEXT] In no event shall more than two (2) members of the Board of Trustees serve at the same time who are employed by the same organization or entity, including affiliated or related entities. Additionally, in no event shall more than two (2) members of the Board of Trustees serve at the same time who represent the same advisory or community board. A third party (or parties) may not select a majority of the total number of Board members or a majority of the non-patient Board members. A Board member selected by a third party may not serve as the Chairperson of the Board of Trustees. A majority of the Executive Committee may not be comprised of Board members selected by a third party.

[TEXT] Section 3. Term and Replacements. Members of the Board of Trustees shall be able to serve a maximum of nine (9) years consecutively: three (3) terms of three (3) years each. After each three- year term, the Governance Committee of the Board shall review the member's attendance and participation to determine whether the member shall be nominated for an additional three (3) year term upon the formal nomination and vote by the Board of Trustees. Consideration for Board membership after nine (9) years of service may occur after a twelve (12) month board service sabbatical by the Trustee. At such time, the Trustee may be eligible to be nominated to the full Board for vote.

[TEXT] Members of the Board of Trustees shall serve staggered terms so that the term of office of one- third of the members will expire at the end of each fiscal year.

[TEXT] Section 4. Election of Members. Election of new members of the Board of Trustees shall be held at the last Board meeting of the fiscal year or at such other time as the Board shall determine.

[TEXT] Board Bylaws

[TEXT] Approved 06/24/2024

========== PAGE 111 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242744

[TEXT] Grant Number: 6 H80CS00087-24-05

[TEXT] Section 5. Vacancies. Any vacancy occurring in the Board of Trustees shall be filled according to the procedures outlined in Section 3. For Trustees filling unexpired terms, if that term is starting any other time than April, shall have their individual term officially begin at the start of the following fiscal year. In the event of a vacancy due to resignation, death or removal, the Board shall fill such vacancy at a duly constituted meeting of the Board of Trustees. New board members, who are filling a new seat, will start on the Board immediately upon election and their official term will begin April 1. At that point, they will be eligible to serve 3, 3-year terms.

[TEXT] Section 6. Removal. Any member of the Board of Trustees may be removed, with or without cause, by two-thirds vote of the other members of the Board of Trustees at a duly constituted meeting of the Board of Trustees. The reasons for possible removal from the Board include, but are not limited to:

[TEXT] · Noncompliance with attendance requirements

[TEXT] • Conduct detrimental to the interests of the Corporation

[TEXT] • Conviction of a heinous or violent crime

[TEXT] • The board member is suspended or debarred from participation in federal programs.

[TEXT] A Board member may voluntarily resign by submitting a written notice to the Chairperson of the Board or their designee.

[TEXT] Section 7. Compensation. The Board of Trustees shall serve without compensation except that they may, at their discretion and by a majority vote of their members, reimburse any or all members for reasonable expenses actually incurred by them in attending meetings or otherwise carrying out their duties to the Corporation.

[TEXT] Section 8. Standards of Conduct. Each member of the Board of Trustees has a fiduciary duty and duty of loyalty to the Corporation and his or her actions must be in the best interests of the Corporation. As such, each member of the Board of Trustees, as well as employees or agents of the Corporation, shall be required to comply with Corporation's Standards of Conduct, as it exists and is amended from time to time, (the "Standards of Conduct") addressing real or potential conflicts of interest, confidentiality, gifts and other matters. Upon request, Trustees, employees and other agents of the Corporation shall sign a document(s) agreeing to the terms of the Standards of Conduct and/or disclosing real or potential conflicts of interest.

[TEXT] The Board of Trustees shall assure policies and systems are in place to assure there is no real or apparent conflict of interest by employees, consultants, and others in the procurement of supplies, property, equipment and services procured with federal funds.

[TEXT] Section 9. Collective Action. The Board shall act in a collective manner pursuant to the provisions of the Board Bylaws. Board members may not attempt to exercise individual authority except as explicitly set forth in the Board Bylaws. Board members may not speak or act individually for the organization unless authorized by the full Board or the CEO. An individual board member may not obligate the organization financially unless authorized by a vote of the full Board.

[TEXT] Board Bylaws

[TEXT] Approved 06/24/2024

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242744

[TEXT] Grant Number: 6 H80CS00087-24-05

[HEADING] ARTICLE III. MEETINGS

[TEXT] Section 1. Regular Meetings. The Board of Trustees shall hold monthly meetings for which minutes shall be kept. The regular meetings of the Board of Trustees shall be held at times and places designated by the Board and shall be so fixed as to ensure that it will be reasonably convenient for all representatives to attend. Regular monthly meetings shall be held at the office of the Chief Executive Officer unless otherwise directed by the Board. If the Board of Trustees shall fail to designate the time and place of the regular meetings, they shall be held on the fourth Monday of each month at 5:30 p.m.

[TEXT] Participation by telephone or videoconference is allowed so long as all Trustees who are participating in the meeting can hear all other Trustees. Such participation shall qualify as "attendance" for purposes of these Bylaws.

[TEXT] Section 2. Special Meetings. Special meetings of the Board of Trustees may be called at any time by the Chairperson or by any four (4) Trustees. The person or persons authorized to call meetings of the Board may fix any place as the place for holding any special meetings of the Board called by them, and such place shall be fixed to ensure that it will be reasonably convenient for all representatives to attend.

[TEXT] Section 3. Notice of Meeting. Notice of any meeting of the Board of Trustees shall be in writing, sent by mail to the last known address of each Trustee, or sent by electronic mail. Such notice shall be deemed to be delivered when deposited in the United States mail with postage thereon prepaid, or sent by electronic mail, at least three (3) calendar days prior to the meeting. An agenda shall be sent to each member at least three (3) calendar days prior to the meeting.

[TEXT] Section 4. Quorum. A simple majority of the members currently serving as Board of Trustees shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of business of any meeting of the Board.

[TEXT] Section 5. Voting Rights. Proxy voting is prohibited. Trustees shall vote by written ballot on any issue when requested by six (6) members of the Board of Trustees. Electronic voting is allowable in all cases where voting is required. Each Trustee shall be entitled to one (1) vote.

[TEXT] Section 6. Adjourned Meeting. Any meeting of the Board of Trustees or any Committee of the Board of Trustees may, by majority vote, be adjourned to a time and place specific; provided, however, when a meeting is adjourned for fifteen (15) days or more, notice of the adjourned meeting shall be given as in the case of an original meeting. When a meeting is adjourned for less than fifteen (15) days, it is not necessary to give any notice of the time and place of the adjourned meeting or of the business to be transacted thereat other than by announcement of the meeting to which the adjournment is taken.

[TEXT] Section 7. Executive Sessions. Executive Sessions may be called at any time during a duly constituted Board of Trustees meeting by the Chairperson or by any four (4) Trustees. All persons who are not board members shall leave the meeting during the Executive Session unless requested by the Board to remain in attendance. The deliberations and discussions during the Executive

[TEXT] Session will not be recorded in the official board minutes. The Board must reconvene in regular session for votes to be taken. Executive Sessions will be called to discuss plans to purchase property,-personnel matters and litigation issues involving the Corporation.

[TEXT] Section 8. Minutes. Minutes are taken at all board meetings. Meeting minutes are approved by the full Board at the next duly called meeting or no later than 60 days after the meeting and signed by the Board Chairperson and Secretary after the Board's approval. Board meeting minutes from the most recent three years will be stored at the organization's corporate offices.

[HEADING] ARTICLE IV. OFFICERS

[TEXT] Section 1. Officers. The officers of the Corporation shall be a Chairperson, a Vice-Chairperson, a Secretary, a Treasurer and such other officers as may be elected by the Board. The officers shall have the authority and responsibility ordinarily given them by custom and usage, or as assigned by the Board of Trustees. Officers shall be elected from the membership of the Board of Trustees.

[HEADING] Section 2. Election and Term of Office.

[TEXT] a. Election. The officers of the Corporation shall be elected annually by the Board of Trustees at the last meeting of the fiscal year or at such other time as the Board shall determine. Nominations shall be submitted to the Board by the Governance Committee.

[TEXT] b. Term of Office. Officers shall be elected to serve for a term of one (1) year or until their successors have been duly elected and qualified, whichever shall last occur. Officers may serve no more than three (3) consecutive terms of office.

[TEXT] c. Officer Vacancy. An officer may resign their office through written notification to the Chairperson of the Board or the CEO. In the event of a vacancy due to resignation, death or removal, the Board shall fill such vacancy at a duly constituted meeting of the Board of Trustees. A Trustee elected to fill a vacancy shall be elected for the unexpired term of their predecessor in office.

[TEXT] Section 3. Board Officer Removal. Any officer elected by the Board of Trustees may be removed, with or without cause, by a two-thirds vote of the members of the Board of Trustees present at any duly called meeting of the Board when, in the judgment of the Board, the best interest of the Corporation would be served thereby. Notice of any such proposed removal shall be given in the agenda for the meeting at which the removal vote shall take place.

[TEXT] Section 4. Chairperson. The Chairperson shall preside at all meetings of the Board of Trustees. The Chairperson shall appoint the Chairpersons and members of standing and ad-hoc committees other than the Executive Committee. The Chairperson may sign, with any other proper officer of the Corporation authorized by the Board of Trustees, any deeds, mortgages, bonds, contracts, or other instruments which the Board of Trustees has authorized to be executed. The Chairperson shall perform such other duties as from time to time may be assigned by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] Section 5. Vice-Chairperson. In the absence of the Chairperson or in the event of the Chairperson's inability or refusal to act, the Vice-Chairperson shall perform the duties of the Chairperson, and when so acting, shall have all the powers of and be subject to all the restrictions upon the Chairperson. The Vice-Chairperson shall perform such other duties as from time to time may be assigned by the Chairperson or by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] Section 6. Secretary. The Secretary shall be responsible for overseeing, or carrying out, the secretarial functions of the Board. The Secretary shall: (a) keep the minutes of the meetings of the Board of Trustees and Executive Committee; (b) see that all notices are duly given in accordance with the provision of these Bylaws or as required by law; (c) be custodian of the Corporation records and of the seal of the Corporation and see that the seal of the Corporation is affixed to all documents, the execution of which on behalf of the Corporation under its seal is duly authorized; and (d) perform all duties incident to the office of Secretary and such other duties as from time to time may be assigned to the Secretary by the Chairperson or by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] Section 7. Treasurer. The Treasurer shall be responsible for working with the Corporation's Chief Financial Officer to oversee the financial affairs of the Corporation. The Treasurer shall: (a) review the financial condition of the Corporation on a monthly basis and report on said condition at the monthly Board of Trustees meetings; (b) chair the Finance Committee of the Board of Trustees; and (c) in general perform all of the duties incident to the office of Treasurer and such other duties as from time to time may be assigned to the Treasurer by the Chairperson or by the Board of Trustees, or by these Bylaws.

[HEADING] ARTICLE V. STANDING COMMITTEES

[TEXT] Section 1. Creation. The Board of Trustees shall, at the last meeting of the fiscal year, determine, designate the following committees with responsibilities as hereinafter designated.

[TEXT] Board committees may be augmented with advisory members, in specific circumstances, as determined by a vote of the full governing board. Advisory members are community members and business experts who volunteer to assist a Standing or Ad-Hoc Committees. Advisory members shall not serve as Trustees and shall have no voting authority on behalf of the full governing board or otherwise serve as fiduciaries and policy makers on behalf of the Corporation. Advisory members cannot serve as Chair of a Standing Committee or serve on the Executive Committee. Committees may meet jointly as needed to fulfill the mission of the organization.

[TEXT] a. Executive Committee: The minimum number of Trustees constituting the Executive Committee shall be five (5). The Trustees constituting the Executive Committee shall be the officers of the Corporation and the Chairpersons of the other Standing Committees. The immediate past Chairperson of the Corporation shall be a member of the Executive Committee; or has the option to serve on the Executive Committee, if they are a member of the Board of Trustees. The officers of the Corporation shall serve in those capacities on the Executive Committee. The Executive Committee shall have and may exercise all the authority of the Board of Trustees in the management of the Corporation during the interim periods between meetings of the Board of Trustees, except as otherwise provided by law or

[TEXT] Section 4. Removal. Any members of Standing Committees may be removed at any time with or without cause by a majority vote of the members of the Board of Trustees or Executive Committee voting at a regular or special meeting. Any non-Trustee or Advisory member can be removed from a committee at any time with or without cause by the Chairperson of the Board of Trustees. Any member of the Executive Committee may be removed at any time with or without cause, by a majority vote of the members of the Board of Trustees voting at a regular or special meeting.

[TEXT] Section 5. Meeting. Meetings of committees shall be held periodically as designated by Chairpersons of the Committees. Special meetings of the Executive Committee or any other committee may be called at any time by the Chairperson of the Board of Trustees, the Chairperson of the Committee or any two (2) members of the Committee.

[HEADING] ARTICLE VI. REQUIRED ATTENDANCE AND SERVICE ON COMMITTEES

[TEXT] To ensure continuity in the management of the affairs of the Corporation, it shall be the responsibility of each member of the Board of Trustees to regularly attend meetings of the Board of Trustees and to serve on at least one (1) committee.

[TEXT] Section 1. Board of Trustees Meetings. Failure of any member of the Board of Trustees to attend three (3) consecutive duly called and convened meetings of the Board of Trustees, or failure to attend at least 50% of the duly called and convened meetings of the Board of Trustees during any fiscal year, shall immediately cause removal of said Trustee from the Board.

[TEXT] Section 2. Board of Trustees Committee Meetings. Failure of any member of the Board of Trustees to attend three (3) consecutive duly called and convened committee meetings, or failure to attend at least 50% of the duly called and convened committee meetings during any fiscal year, shall be subject to removal from the Board.

[TEXT] Section 3. Reinstatement. A member of the Board of Trustees who has been removed due to absences may petition the Board of Trustees for reinstatement within 30 days of their removal, which reinstatement shall not be retroactive. A letter of petition will be submitted to the Governance Committee for their consideration.

[HEADING] ARTICLE VII. CONTRACTS, LOANS, CHECKS AND DEPOSITS

[TEXT] Section 1. Contracts. The Board of Trustees may authorize any officer or officers, agent or agents, to enter into any contract or execute and deliver any instrument in the name of and on behalf of the Corporation, and authority may be general or confined to specific instances.

[TEXT] Section 2. Loans. No loans shall be contracted on behalf of the Corporation and no evidence of indebtedness shall be issued in its name unless authorized by a resolution of the Board of Trustees. Such authority may be general or confined to specific instances.

[TEXT] Section 3. Checks and Drafts. All checks, drafts, or other orders for the payment of money, issued in the name of the Corporation, shall be signed by such officer or officers, agent or agencies of the

[HEADING] ARTICLE VIII. DUTIES OF THE BOARD OF TRUSTEES

[TEXT] Section 1. Responsibility of Board of Trustees. The Board of Trustees shall have the authority to manage the business and affairs of the Corporation pursuant to the Board Bylaws. Specifically, the Board of Trustees shall:

[TEXT] a. Approve the selection and dismissal of the Chief Executive Officer (CEO)

[TEXT] b. Review annually the performance of the Chief Executive Officer

[TEXT] c. Create and maintain a three to five (3-5) year Strategic Plan

[TEXT] d. Establish, adopt, and review the following written policies every three years:

[TEXT] · Human Resources policies, including those addressing selection and dismissal procedures, salary and benefit scales, employee grievance procedures, and equal opportunity practices.

[TEXT] · Financial management policies and practices including a system to assure accountability for center resources, a process for long range financial planning, and set eligibility criteria for discount fee plans; periodically reviewing the financial status of the health center and the results of the annual audit to ensure appropriate follow-up actions are taken; adopting policy for eligibility of services including criteria for partial payment schedules.

[TEXT] · Healthcare policies including scope and availability of services, location and hours of services, The Board shall approve sub-awarding or contracting for a substantial portion of the approved services, if required.

[TEXT] · Adopting health care policies including quality of care audit procedures.

[TEXT] · Confidentiality policies to ensure the protection of proprietary and other corporate information received by members of the Board of Trustees and employees, independent contractors, consultants, and other individuals who can receive such information.

[TEXT] · Conflict of interest and other policies as determined necessary by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] · Ensure a process is developed for hearing and resolving patient grievances.

[TEXT] e. Approve applications related to the health center project, including approving the annual budget which outlines the proposed uses of both federal Health Center Program award and non-federal resources and revenue.

[TEXT] f. Develop its overall plan for the Health Center program project.

[TEXT] g. Provide direction for long-range planning, including but not limited to identifying health center priorities and adopting a three-year plan for financial management and capital expenditures.

[TEXT] h. Assess the achievement of project objectives through evaluation of health center activities, including service utilization patterns, productivity (efficiency and effectiveness) of the center and patient satisfaction.

[TEXT] i. Ensure that a process is developed for hearing and resolving patient grievances.

[TEXT] j. Oversee of the selection of independent auditor and adoption of annual audit.

[TEXT] k. Ensure the Corporation is operating in compliance with Federal, State, and local laws and

[TEXT] Section 2. Appointment of CEO. The Board of Trustees shall appoint the Chief Executive Officer of the Corporation and shall expressly name the CEO as an agent of the Corporation, accountable to the Board of Trustees. In this capacity the CEO may sign, upon resolution of the Board, deeds, mortgages, bonds, contracts, and other instruments which the Board of Trustees has authorized to be executed. The CEO, subject to the oversight of the Board of Trustees, shall have responsibility for the general care, supervision, and direction of Corporation's affairs in furtherance of the policies and programs established by the Board of Trustees. The CEO shall have the authority to employ, supervise, and discharge all personnel in accordance with the policies established by the Board of Trustees. The CEO or his/her designee shall attend all meetings of the Board of Trustees and the Executive Committee, unless the Board requests the CEO's absence during evaluation of the CEO's performance. The CEO shall perform such other duties and exercise such other powers as may be assigned by the Board of Trustees.

[HEADING] ARTICLE IX. GENERAL PROVISIONS

[TEXT] Section 1. Seal. The Seal of the Corporation shall consist of two (2) concentric circles between which is the name of the Corporation and in the center of which is inscribed SEAL: and such Seal, as impressed on the margin hereof, is hereby adopted as the Seal of the Corporation.

[TEXT] Section 2. Waiver of Notice. Whenever any notice is required to be given to any Trustee by law, by the Articles of Incorporation or by these Bylaws, a waiver thereof in writing signed by the person or persons entitled to such notice, whether before or after the time stated therein, shall be equivalent to the giving of such notice.

[TEXT] Section 3. Fiscal Year. The fiscal year of the Corporation shall be fixed by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] Section 4. Amendments. Except as otherwise provided herein, these Bylaws may be amended or repealed, and new Bylaws may be adopted by the affirmative vote of a majority of the Trustees then holding office at any regular or special meetings of the Board of Trustees. Members of the Board of Trustees must be given thirty (30) days written notice of the proposed revisions.

[TEXT] Section 5. Amendments to the Articles of Incorporation. Except as otherwise provided herein, the Corporation's Articles of Incorporation may be amended or repealed, or new Articles may be adopted, by the affirmative vote of a majority of the Trustees then holding office at any regular or special meetings of the Board of Trustees. Members of the Board of Trustees must be given thirty (30) days written notice of the proposed revisions.

[TEXT] Section 6. Parliamentary Procedures. The conduct of all meetings of the Corporation shall be in accord with ROBERT'S RULES OF ORDER, Newly Revised.

[TEXT] Section 7. Board Governance Policies. The Board of Trustees may adopt a Board of Trustees Governance Policy and Procedure Manual, which defines the governance role of the Board and how this role is to be carried out.

[TEXT] Section 8. Dissolution of the Corporation. In the event of dissolution, the residual assets of the Corporation will be turned over to one or more organizations which themselves are exempt organizations described in Section 501 (c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954 as amended or to the federal, state or local government to be used exclusively for public purposes.

[TEXT] Summary: The CEO is the leader of the organization, establishing a vision for Community Impact that is achieved through the efforts of a diverse team of high-performing leaders and staff. The CEO is the Chief Mobilizer, leveraging the power of relationships and networks, and working across private, public, and corporate sectors to improve conditions in the community. The CEO is dedicated to shared and measurable goals for the common good. The CEO is the steward of ACH's brand and understands his/her role in growing and protecting the reputation of ACH.

[TEXT] Essential Duties, Responsibilities, and Functions:

[TEXT] . Responsible for overall impact of ACH on the community.

[TEXT] · Works closely with Board to craft and adapt strategies to achieve increased impact.

[TEXT] . Establishes and builds relationships with top leaders in the community.

[TEXT] · Identifies, cultivates, and solicits prospective donors and new corporate partners; leverages personal and professional contacts and relationships into fundraising opportunities; and promotes a culture of fundraising at the staff and board levels.

[TEXT] . Serves as the principal resource to Board of Trustees and its committees, giving strong direction in policy formulation and interpretation.

[TEXT] · Oversees other key management staff in carrying out the day-to-day activities

[TEXT] · necessary for the proposed project. Partners with Board and Senior Leadership team to craft organizational goals and develops strategies to ensure that they are achieved.

[TEXT] · Ensures coordination and alignment of all ACH activities to strategic direction.

[TEXT] · Accountable for building and leading high-performing teams, ensuring all teams are aligned and collaborating to achieve organizational results.

[TEXT] · Maintains accountability for the operational and fiscal integrity of the organization within policies set by the Board. Assesses organizational capacity to implement strategies and identifies gaps in systems and staffing; directly supervises Senior Leadership positions and establishes individual goals; works with CFO to manage organizational spending, monitor budget compliance, and mitigate financial risks; and ensures that goals of inclusiveness and diversity among staff and volunteers are met.

[TEXT] Qualifications: Required: Undergraduate degree. Training, experience or advanced degree preferred in business, public administration, or not-for-profit management. 7-10 years' experience in a senior strategic leadership role required, 3 years in role may substitute for an advanced degree. Substantial experience working in the nonprofit sector (FQHC experience desirable) and interacting with volunteers and diverse boards. Alternatively, extensive senior strategic leadership experience in management of organizations of comparable size and mission. Expertise on issues relevant to the organization. Experience in or across multiple sectors, including nonprofit, public and corporate environments. Experience in developing partnerships, building teams and conflict management. Experience in building revenue and increasing philanthropic support.

[TEXT] Knowledge, Skills and Abilities: Ability to command confidence and respect of stakeholders. Demonstrated track record of promoting diversity and ability to build collaboration with the community at large. Must demonstrate a high level of intelligence and intellectual curiosity and a desire to explore new ideas and innovative approaches to solving problems. Unquestioned integrity; a long term perspective; a strong sense of accountability; a practical ability to get things done; wisdom and good judgment; a fair and thoughtful approach to management, combined with the flexibility and courage to shift direction and experiment with new initiatives; excellent verbal and written communication skills; a high energy level and sense of humor.

[TEXT] Attachment 4 - Position Descriptions for Key Management Staff Fiscal Year 2026 Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004 Job Title: Chief Medical Officer (CMO) Department: Clinical Services | Reports To: Chief Executive Officer Work Hours: Full-time, Exempt

[TEXT] Summary: The CMO works in partnership with the CEO to support and facilitate an interdisciplinary team approach to the delivery of quality care to patients, families, and the community by implementing senior team and board initiatives. This is accomplished by creating an environment in which collaboration is valued and excellence in care, service, education, and innovation is promoted and achieved. This position has the responsibilities of providing direct patient care. The CMO will supervise all medical clinicians in the organization.

[HEADING] Essential Duties, Responsibilities, and Functions: Clinical Leadership and Oversight

[TEXT] · Provides leadership for clinical care delivery and ensures adherence to evidence-based guidelines.

[TEXT] · Monitors provider performance, documentation, and quality outcomes.

[TEXT] · Supervises and mentors advanced practice providers in compliance with medical board standards. Patient Care and Quality

[TEXT] · Manages a patient panel aligned with productivity goals and service standards.

[TEXT] · Delivers comprehensive care including acute, chronic, and preventive services.

[TEXT] . Coordinates team-based care with social work, behavioral health, and ancillary staff.

[TEXT] Provider Development

[TEXT] · Coaches and mentors provider staff, fostering accountability and clinical excellence.

[TEXT] · Conducts performance and peer reviews, developing improvement plans as needed.

[TEXT] · Facilitates onboarding, training, and professional growth opportunities.

[TEXT] Quality Improvement and Reporting

[TEXT] · Participates in Quality and Provider meetings and related committees.

[TEXT] · Identifies and addresses performance trends to improve outcomes.

[TEXT] · Prepares quarterly performance and productivity reports for executive leadership. Professional Conduct

[TEXT] · Models organizational values and professionalism.

[TEXT] · Maintains punctuality, effective communication, and commitment to continuous improvement.

[TEXT] Qualifications: Required: MD or DO with current and active license to practice in North Carolina. Current and active BC and DEA licensure/certification and BLS certification. Three years supervisory experience or experience in a leadership role. Current five years of direct primary patient care. Preferred: Primary care experience of all ages. Experience working in a community health/FQHC or outpatient medical facility. Experience in practice management and process improvement. Direct experience working in grant-funded programs. Demonstrated success in process improvement initiatives.

[TEXT] Knowledge, Skills and Abilities: Strong computer skills with knowledge of Microsoft Word, Excel, Outlook. Strong EMR experience and exposure. Broad knowledge of population health management and preventive health screening standards. Demonstrated proficiency in Electronic Health Records and clinical data systems. Ability to effectively present information and speak before groups of employees and outside consultants and respond to questions/comments from the same. Knowledge in primary care practice redesign, Patient Centered Medical Home principles, Advance Medical Home, and continuous clinical quality improvement methodologies. Knowledge of chronic disease management and appropriate interventions managing disease processes.

[TEXT] Attachment 5 - Biographical Sketches for Key Management Staff Fiscal Year 2026 New Access Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[TEXT] Chief Executive Officer - Scot McCray, MPH

[TEXT] Scot McCray has served as the Chief Executive Officer of ACH since April 2021. He began his career in Camden, New Jersey, where he led strategic initiatives that helped shape the city's nationally recognized economic, health care, and public safety reforms.

[TEXT] With more than 20 years of leadership experience, Mr. McCray has advanced the growth and performance of Federally Qualified Health Centers (FQHCs), integrated networks, and Accountable Care Organizations (ACOs). He is widely regarded as a visionary leader and market disruptor, bringing business acumen, advocacy, and collaboration to the organizations and communities he serves.

[TEXT] Mr. McCray earned a Bachelor of Science in Public Health and Health Science from Clemson University and a Master of Public Health in Health Systems, Policy, and Administration from the University of Medicine and Dentistry of New Jersey School of Public Health.

[TEXT] Currently, Mr. McCray serves as the Vice Chair of the North Carolina Community Health Center Association Board of Directors and Chair of the Governing Committee.

[TEXT] Chief Medical Officer - Colin Ottey, M.D.

[TEXT] Dr. Colin Ottey serves as the Chief Medical Officer of ACH, where he provides clinical leadership, strategic oversight, and guidance to ensure the delivery of high-quality, patient-centered care. An internal medicine physician with more than 25 years of clinical and leadership experience, Dr. Ottey is deeply committed to advancing health equity and improving outcomes for medically underserved communities.

[TEXT] Originally from Jamaica, Dr. Ottey earned his undergraduate degree from Brooklyn College before completing his medical education at the University of Illinois-Chicago College of Medicine in 1994. He has since dedicated his career to primary care and population health, with a strong focus on reducing health disparities and addressing the complex needs of diverse patient populations.

[TEXT] At ACH, Dr. Ottey plays a vital role in strengthening care coordination, integrating behavioral health and enabling services, and expanding service delivery sites to meet growing community needs. He is widely recognized for his patient-first approach, collaborative leadership style, and commitment to fostering innovation and excellence in community-based health care.

[TEXT] Chief Financial Officer - Tiffany Robertson, MBA

[TEXT] Tiffany Robertson joined ACH as Interim Chief Financial Officer in June 2022 and brings a wealth of expertise in nonprofit, health care, and consulting finance. She is a highly regarded financial leader with specialized excellence in accounting, fiscal management, and business operations, and is recognized for her ability to deliver results in complex, deadline-driven environments.

[TEXT] Ms. Robertson holds a Bachelor of Science in Accounting and Economics and a Master of Business Administration. She has also served as a Federal Grant Reviewer for the Health Resources and Services Administration, where she evaluated and scored applications from Federally Qualified Health Centers, Primary Care Associations, and Health Center Controlled Networks.

Since 1972, Advance Community Health has delivered high-quality, comprehensive health care to our community. The work of Advance Community Health's dedicated staff provides health care services to many residents who, without the health center, would have limited access to care.

With federal grant support, Advance Community Health is able to provide comprehensive health care services that improve outcomes for residents across its service area. By increasing access to comprehensive primary care and prevention in a family practice setting, the organization's health center helps to ensure that patients are able to seek care earlier and avoid more serious, sometimes life-threatening health consequences which require more costly medical interventions.

[TEXT] Dear Mr. McCray,

[TEXT] Advance Community Health and Lincoln Community Health Center (LCHC) have worked collaboratively to meet the needs of Durham and Wake Counties. This partnership has served to increase access to services to local residents. Lincoln fully supports Advance Community Health's receipt of federal Section 330 funding.

[TEXT] The collaboration between our organizations meets a number of needs for low-income and uninsured residents in the community. Lincoln provides primary care (Pediatrics, Adult, and Family Medicine), behavioral health, medication assisted treatment, dental, health education, case management, substance use, pharmacy, laboratory, and radiology services to residents. Advance Community Health provides high-quality healthcare services that include primary care, substance use care, dental care, as well as case management and health education. Because of the high prevalence of poverty in our area, these services are critical to meeting the healthcare needs of the population. The collaborative relationship between our two organizations has helped identify the needs of patients and ensure access to services that meet those needs. Together with other community partner organizations, Advance Community Health plays a key part in improving the health, well-being, and overall quality of life for area residents.

[TEXT] LCHC considers Advance Community Health's provision of affordable healthcare services as invaluable to the region, and we look forward to continuing our collaboration. LCHC fully supports Advance Community Health's application for Section 330 funding.

[TEXT] Dear Mr. McCray,

[TEXT] Piedmont Health would like to offer its full support for Advance Community Health's application for federal Section 330 Service Area Competition (SAC, HRSA-26-004). Since 1972, Advance Community Health has delivered high-quality, comprehensive health care to our community. The work of Advance Community Health's dedicated staff provides health care services to many residents who, without the health center, would have limited access to care.

[TEXT] Like Advance Community Health, Piedmont Health also works to serve local residents and understands not only the great need in the area, but also the role and impact of community service organizations. For years, our organizations, along with others, have worked in partnership to meet local needs, whether they be social or medical. Each community organization has its role, and that shared responsibility and willingness to work together has served to improve the overall wellbeing of the population. Advance's role in particular has improved the health of residents through the provision not only of primary care, but also preventative screenings, health education and the promotion of a healthy lifestyle. By improving the daily health of residents, Advance lowers the risk of complications of serious, often life-threatening diseases and therefore reduces the need for and cost of providing acute care - a valuable service for the community as a whole but especially for the uninsured and low-income residents otherwise unable to afford medical care.

[TEXT] Piedmont Health is proud to continue sharing this responsibility through an ongoing mutual referral relationship with Advance and through continued collaboration in identifying and meeting local needs. As such, Piedmont Health believes strongly that the provision of Section 330 funding to Advance Community Health will have a positive impact in Wake and Franklin counties.

[TEXT] Sincerely, 200 Daniella Jaimes-Colina, PhD Chief Executive Officer
