[TEXT] Attachment 13: Health Center Program Compliance Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[HEADING] Sliding Fee Discount Program

[TEXT] Compliant; Required Attachments and Forms: Attachment 10: Sliding Fee Discount Schedule(s), Form 5A: Services Provided

[HEADING] Compliance Narrative:

[TEXT] Describe the following aspects of the SFDP: Uniform applicability to all patients. Definitions of income and family. Alignment with the current FPG. Methods for assessing all patients for sliding fee discount eligibility based only on income and family size. Assurance that patient charges are adjusted based on ability to pay and consistent with the SFDS. Policies related to nominal charges for patients with incomes at or below 100 percent of the current FPG.

[TEXT] How you assess all patients for sliding fee discount eligibility based only on income and family size. See income definition in Chapter 9: Sliding Fee Discount Program of the Compliance Manual.

[TEXT] ACH provides services according to a Board approved SFDP based solely on income and family size, consistent with Chapter 9 of HRSA's Compliance Manual. The SFDS applies to patients with incomes up to 200% of the FPG.

[TEXT] ACH utilizes written policies and procedures to implement the SFDS. These policies and procedures define income and family size, specify documentation or verification requirements for determining and recording family size and income, detail the specific structure for the SFDS itself, establish the frequency for re-evaluation of patient eligibility, and address provisions for waiving fees and nominal charges for specific patient circumstances.

[TEXT] Family size and income are verified using official documentation to determine wages and salary, excluding assets and other similar items, consistent with HRSA definitions. These figures are compared to the annually published FPG. ACH follows HRSA's definition of "family," which is a group of two or more persons related by birth, marriage, or adoption who live together; all such related persons are considered members of one family.

[TEXT] Eligibility determinations are conducted respectfully, confidentially, and in a culturally appropriate manner to avoid barriers to care. Acceptable income documentation includes recent pay stubs, tax returns, or other verifiable proof of earnings; assets are not considered.

[TEXT] All patients are made aware of the SFDP via the Patient Registration Form, which is completed by all new patients, and updated annually. Signs in multiple languages are posted near the front desk area of all locations providing information about the SFDP. When patients inquire about or are invited to apply for the Sliding Fee Discount Program, front-office staff and Patient Financial Navigators provide assistance with completing the application. Applications are reviewed and updated annually, or sooner if there is a change in household income or size. For patients who are unemployed, report zero income, or are homeless or transitioning from homelessness, eligibility is re-evaluated every six months to ensure continued accuracy.

[TEXT] Advance Community Health, Inc. H80CS00087

[TEXT] 2



========== PAGE 151 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242744

[TEXT] Grant Number: 6 H80CS00087-24-05

[TEXT] Attachment 13: Health Center Program Compliance Service Area Competition HRSA-26-004

[TEXT] Patients without income documentation may self-declare income for one visit per year; documentation must be provided at the next visit or the patient is classified as self-pay.

[TEXT] For homeless individuals, ACH follows Section 330 of the Public Health Service Act (42 U.S.C. § 254b) and Bureau of Primary Health Care definitions of homelessness. Per guidance, an individual may be considered homeless if they are "doubled up" with others, or if they are a previously homeless person being discharged from a hospital, prison, or similar institution without stable housing to return to. All patients who identify as homeless, regardless of insurance status, must provide documentation of their homeless status consistent with this definition. Acceptable documentation includes a certification letter from a shelter or social service agency or correlating verification forms such as household instability or "doubled-up" documentation. This documentation is attached to the patient's SFDP application to ensure eligibility determination aligns with HRSA requirements.

[TEXT] ACH's Practice Management System calculates the percentage of FPG based on income and family size and flags records for review. Eligibility is re-verified annually, and the Chief Financial Officer and Practice Managers audit files to ensure accuracy and adherence to policy.

[TEXT] How you adjust patient charges based on the ability to pay. ACH adjusts patient charges based on ability to pay through its Board-approved SFDP. Discounts are applied using a SFDS aligned with the most recent FPG and determined by verified household income and family size.

[TEXT] The SFDP applies to all individuals and families with annual incomes between 100% and 200% of the FPG. Discounts (flat or percentage-based) are applied consistently across all service types, including medical, behavioral health, dental, nursing, nutrition, pharmacy, urgent care, integrated care, and OB/GYN.

[TEXT] Patients with annual incomes at or below 100% of the FPG are charged only a nominal fee, while those between 101% and 200% of the FPG receive graduated discounts. The SFDS includes four pay classes above 100% FPG - 101-125%, 126-150%, 151-175%, and 176-200%. No sliding fee discount is approved for individuals or families with incomes exceeding 200% of the FPG.

[TEXT] All services are billed at their full established charge, and discounts are applied according to each patient's verified eligibility level. Uninsured patients and those who are underinsured (with self-pay balances such as co-payments or deductibles) are encouraged to apply for the SFDP.

[TEXT] Eligibility is determined and documented annually, based on verification of income and household size, and reassessed whenever a change in financial circumstances occurs. ACH ensures that no patient is denied care due to inability to pay, thereby maintaining equitable access to all health center services.

[TEXT] Each year, the Board of Trustees, comprised of a patient-majority membership, reviews and approves the SFDS to incorporate the most recent FPG. As part of this review, the Board evaluates the structure and effectiveness of the discount schedule to ensure it continues to reduce financial barriers to care. This includes reviewing UDS data, practice management system financial reports, and patient

[TEXT] satisfaction survey results to assess whether patients across all discount pay classes are accessing care.

[TEXT] In conjunction with this annual review, ACH's policies and procedures governing implementation of the sliding fee scale are also reviewed and updated as needed to ensure continued compliance with HRSA's Sliding Fee Discount Program requirements.

[TEXT] Whether you have a nominal charge for patients with incomes at or below 100% of the FPG. ACH applies a nominal flat fee for patients with incomes at or below 100% of the FPG and does not reflect the cost of the service provided. The nominal fee is intended solely to encourage shared responsibility and not to create a financial barrier to care. Examples (effective 05/01/2025-03/31/2026) include: $40 for medical or behavioral health visits; $60 for dental visits; $10 for nurse visits; $17 for nutrition services; $10.50 for pharmacy dispensing; $125 for urgent care visits; $75 for integrated care visits; and Fee per procedure for OB/GYN.

[TEXT] · The applicability of all Health Center Program requirements to the subrecipient.

[TEXT] · The applicability to the subrecipient of any distinct statutory, regulatory, and policy requirements of other Federal programs associated with their HRSA- approved scope of project. That all costs paid for by the Federal subaward are allowable consistent with Federal Cost Principles.

[TEXT] ACH enters into contracts and subawards as necessary to support the delivery of required and additional services within its approved scope of project (Forms 5A and 5B). All contracts and agreements are executed in accordance with ACH's Contracts and Subawards Policy, which ensures compliance with federal procurement standards (45 CFR Part 75 Subpart D) and includes provisions for conflict of interest, cost reasonableness, and documentation of services rendered.

[TEXT] Only the CEO and individuals specifically authorized in writing may bind ACH to contractual relationships. The Finance Department maintains centralized records of all contracts, and the CFO oversees fiscal and compliance monitoring of each agreement. Where appropriate, ACH consults with external legal counsel to ensure that all contracts comply with applicable federal, state, and local laws as well as funding-source requirements.

[HEADING] Billing and Collections

[HEADING] Compliant; Required Attachments and Forms: Form 3: Income Analysis

[HEADING] Compliance Narrative:

[TEXT] Describe how you conduct billing and collections, including:

[TEXT] · Your participation in Medicare, Medicaid, Children's Health Insurance Program (CHIP) and as appropriate, other public or private assistance programs or health insurance, as applicable. This description should be supported by Form 3: Income Analysis.

[TEXT] · Your board-approved policies, as well as your procedures for waiving or reducing fees, to ensure that fees or payments will be waived or reduced based on specific circumstances due to any patient's inability to pay.

[TEXT] ACH participates in Medicare, Medicaid, and the North Carolina Health Choice (CHIP) programs, as well as a wide range of commercial and managed care insurance plans. Trained Outreach and Enrollment Specialists and Patient Financial Navigators assist patients in enrolling in public and private coverage programs, including Marketplace plans, ensuring equitable access to care regardless of income or insurance status.

[TEXT] Billing and collections are centralized within the Finance Department, which oversees insurance verification, charge capture, claims submission, payment posting, and follow-up. ACH utilizes Epic as its electronic health record and patient accounting system, integrated with a clearinghouse for electronic claims submission and remittance processing. Standardized billing workflows and payer-specific protocols ensure accuracy, compliance, and timely reimbursement.

[TEXT] ACH maintains board-approved Billing and Collections and SFDP policies to ensure that inability to pay is never a barrier to care. All patients are assessed for SFDP eligibility based on household income and family size, consistent with FPG. Fees are waived or reduced according to the SFDS, which is reviewed and approved annually by the Board of Trustees.

[TEXT] In accordance with HRSA requirements, no patient is denied services due to inability to pay. To prevent financial hardship, ACH works with patients to establish affordable payment plans when needed. When nominal fees pose a burden, waivers or alternative arrangements may be approved by the Chief Executive Officer, Chief Financial Officer, Chief Operating Officer, Chief Medical Officer, or Director of Patient Financial Services, based on requests from practice managers or providers.

[TEXT] These systems and policies ensure compliance with HRSA and federal regulations, maintain revenue integrity, and uphold ACH's mission to provide affordable, accessible, and equitable care to all patients regardless of their ability to pay.

[TEXT] Article II - Section 2 - Board of Trustees/ Numbers and Qualifications

[TEXT] The board shall have at least nine (9) and no more than seventeen (17) members. However, the size can increase to a maximum of twenty- five (25) members if it becomes necessary to accommodate additional practice sites, communities, or specific expertise.

[TEXT] At least 51 percent of Board Members are patients served by the health center.

[TEXT] Article II, Section 2 - Board of Trustees/ Numbers and Qualifications

[TEXT] At least fifty-one percent (51%) of board members shall be patients who shall be representative of the Corporation's patient demographics in terms of age, race, ethnicity, and gender.

[TEXT] At least fifty-one percent (51%) of board members shall be patients who shall be representative of the Corporation's patient demographics in terms of age, race, ethnicity, and gender. The patient board members shall be representative of the various practice locations and communities served and shall be selected in keeping with federal rules and regulations that govern the funding and administration of healthcare centers.

[TEXT] Article II, Section 2 - Board of Trustees/ Numbers and Qualifications

[TEXT] No more than fifty percent (50%) of the non- patient Trustees may be individuals who derive greater than 10% of their annual income from the healthcare industry. Specifically, "individuals" who derive their income from the healthcare industry" are defined as persons currently employed in organizations that provide primary healthcare, specialty services, hospital or rehabilitative services, including solo or private practice. The definition does not include persons retired from those organizations.

[TEXT] Health center employees and immediate family members (i.e., spouses, children, parents, or siblings through blood, adoption, or marriage) of employees may not be health center board members.

[TEXT] Article II, Section 2 - Board of Trustees/ Numbers and Qualifications

[TEXT] No member of the Board of Trustees shall be an employee of the Corporation or be related by blood, marriage, or adoption to an employee of the Corporation. The definition of 'relative' for purposes of the Board of Trustees includes spouse, parents, children, siblings, aunts, uncles, grandparents, domestic partners, or persons in these roles through adoption or marriage.

[TEXT] Activity/Location Information

[TEXT] Type of Activity

[TEXT] Immunizations

[TEXT] Frequency of Activity

[TEXT] Periodic according to seasonal needs

[TEXT] Description of Activity

[TEXT] Advance Community Health practices offer routine childhood and adult immunizations to include influenza and pneumonia vaccines as part of their preventative health mission. During influenza season and school preparation times, additional services are offered to ensure that as many individuals receive appropriate immunizations as possible. Services are extended through walk-in clinics to non-Advance Community Health clients at these times as part of community outreach.

[TEXT] Type of Location(s) where Activity is Conducted

[TEXT] Advance Community Health medical/dental practices, churches, community centers, homeless shelters and other civic locations as appropriate.

[TEXT] Type of Activity

[TEXT] Non-Clinical Outreach

[TEXT] Frequency of Activity

[TEXT] Daily during COVID-19 Pandemic

[TEXT] Description of Activity

[TEXT] ACH staff will screen homeless individuals entering the Oak City Cares building. ACH has its Homeless Program onsite at Oak City Cares. Many of the services in the Oak City Cares facility have been closed due to the pandemic. The Oak City Cares facility has showers and laundry facilities for the homeless, and Advance will screen individuals coming to the facility to determine whether they have COVID symptoms prior to entering. If the person has COVID symptoms, they will be sent to the Advance clinic for testing. If the person does not show any signs of the virus, they will be allowed into the

[TEXT] Type of Location(s) where Activity is Conducted

[TEXT] Oak City Cares building which is an outreach site for Advance's HCH program.

[TEXT] Frequency of Activity

[TEXT] Occassionally

[TEXT] Description of Activity

[TEXT] Advance Community Health nurses and registered dieticians participate in health fairs and community outreach events to provide chronic disease screening and preventive education. Nurses and registered dieticians will provide health screenings and health education. Patients who do not have a primary care provider will be referred to an Advance Community Health location. Staff are able to make follow-up appointments, using laptops, at the remote locations.
